RATING: 7
I tend to enjoy any decent game that can be played solo, and Space Hulk was no exception. It's a fast moving, tactical game that scales in difficulty as the game progresses. It is a little too luck based, in my opinion (a bad streak of dice rolls can crush your winning odds), but it never gets dull. It's a good game, overall, but with low replayability and having to deal with luck, I can't give this game a super high rating.

RATING: 8.5
A clever card implementation of Space Hulk, that manages to capture the claustrophobic and brooding atmosphere of the original miniature game surprisingly well.. and to turn the originally duel-type game into a co-op with up to six players! It even works wonderfully as a solitaire! It's extremely portable and lots of fun to play (although fiendishly hard to beat, like the original!). I'm impressed.

RATING: 8.5
Quick and fast game, which I usually play solo.
The games captures the theme very well (if you have space hulk, you'll recognise all the characters), plays quick and is difficult enough. There's a good amount of randomness, but planning your moves as best as you can is still very important.
All the space marines team are interesting, except for the green team, which I don't like very much.
The expansions add a good amount of variety, but that isn't really needed at the moment, I just bought them because of the expiring license.

RATING: 7
There aren't many games that scale just as well with 6 players as they do with 1.  Largely tactical with a cool theme and just enough randomness on the attack roles to keep things unpredictable.  The game is good value for money and small enough to easily carry to gaming sessions.  My only real criticism is that a couple of the expansion should have been included in the base set for more variety.  Another great solo game and excellent co-op.  Surprised this isn't rated higher on BGG.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Bumping this from 7 to 8 after the second game.  Now that we're playing correctly, the game is really cool.  It has neat mechanics, and it's perfect for a lunch game, since it supports 1-6 players and can be played in an hour.  The manual is complete, but is put together oddly.  As a result, it is difficult to learn the game from the manual.

Update: Kicking this one down to a 6 since it never hits the table any more.  Nobody seems to want to deal with the near-hopelessness.  Also, the manual sucks hard enough that it is really tough to deal with rules questions when they come up.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Death Angel is a difficult game. You'll find yourself losing more often than not, which can be frustrating when playing alone. When playing with others, however, you have someone to share in that panicked tension that this games replicates so well. You know you won't win as often as you lose, but it makes the game exciting, scary, and all the more enjoyable when you finally grasp victory. Solitaire mode works surprisingly well, but failure only serves to frustrate when playing alone.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
This is a good game, but in my opinion it's been surpassed by more elegant solo (and co-op) games in recent years. Sylvion is a great parallel. SHDA just has a ton of random luck, with a lot of your Marines' lives, and your games, hinging on 50/50 rolls. Experience and smart play will reduce those rolls or let you reroll them, but they're still there, and you never get more dice to roll like most dice-based co-ops. It takes up a large amount of table space and playtime compared to the box size, the rulebook is atrocious, one of FFG's worst, and the actual gameplay is just not as compelling for me as most of my other solos. I've given it to a friend indefinitely at this point.

RATING: 8
Happy to have found a reasonably cheap second hand copy of this on facebook. From a solo or 2P point of view, it's more puzzly than I anticipated, it has a slight chess feel when you have to decide on your actions. You get the feeling that there is probably a definite correct choice and that you're not making it! But the theme and sense of movement and action is strong enough that it balances the strategic puzzle side quite nicely. For its quick setup and comic book aesthetic I can see myself playing this a lot over the years to come.

RATING: 8
Very good! The main problems with the game are the logistics around running through the characters in ascending numeric order (only a factor if you play with more than 2) and that the rulebook is quite dense and strangely structured. It's almost impossible to look up a rule since nothing ever seems to be where you would expect it to be.

How well you do is going to be highly influenced by random effects, but the game zips along fast enough that it's not a large issue and there's a pretty reasonable amount of luck mitigation even if it's something which shrinks over the course of the game rather than grows.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It's certainly an interesting game, though not really a great one - it's a hard co-op that doesn't have any fine-tuning levers (which is a strike against it) and a huge reliance on live-or-die dice rolls.  The mechanics kind of suck, to be honest: you're piling Genestealer enemies up against your row of Space Marines and trying to roll skulls to kill them off before they roll big numbers against you.  But there are a pile of player factions with sometimes very interesting abilities, and the card-based action selection mechanism works well.  It's solidly alright+.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Death Angel is fast-paced and action packed.  The engine that runs the Genestealers is challenging enough.  

Which is all just as well because there isn't a whole lot going on in terms of decision-making here.  It's a game of tactical combat that boils down to which of two ways my marines face, a choice of one of two actions per turn and lots of die rolls.  There's no variation in the enemy either; just hoards of them.

Production quality is fine.  The art is disappointing.  Compared to the same company's dark, sinister Doom, Death Angel looks like a cartoon intended for young boys.

RATING: 7.25
Amazing little co-op design - just wish it were harder, that the expansion content were easier to get hold of now it's going out of print, and that the theme was more my style. That variable player powers come as synergistic supplements to base actions shared by all - and fire at different times - adds an enormous amount of character to each team with very little complexity. I also infinitely prefer this game's system of movement to Dungeon crawlers like Descent, in which space is rarely important for reasons other than proximity and consequently contributes very little to base game play. A more complex, thematically richer version of this base design would blow me away, and I'm hoping that due to the quiet success/critical reception of this one post FFG and GW's split FFG might do exactly this.

RATING: 5.997
Death Angel definitely is not the type of game that I normally get into, but it is a really fun game for solo play. Many solo games feel very puzzley, but the randomness in this game (dice rolling, random rooms, and the event cards) allows for interesting tactical decisions with no guarantee of success. I definitely wouldn't want to play this game all the time because of the large amount of luck, but it stays in my solo-game rotation because it offers something unique in my collection.

Update: I love the tension of the game. I am typically on the edge of my seat, but I ended up getting rid of it because it just had too much luck for me to enjoy on a regular basis.

RATING: 7
I actually like this game more than I thought I would; which is especially noteworthy considering that I'm usually luke-warm on this type of sci-fi. I like it much more at $10 than at $15-$20, but either way you get a solid little game inside this box. A popular choice for solo play, it's great for travel or those nights when you're too lazy or tired to commit to something larger. You get to manipulate cards, tokens, and a die, with minimal setup and a reasonable yet satisfying game length. The rules can seem a bit bewildering at first if you've never seen it played, but once you play it, their simplicity becomes evident and referencing the rule book always yields the desired clarification. Sufficiently engaging and very convenient, Death Angel earns its small spot on your shelf.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Initial Impressions: This card game really captures the essence of the Space Hulk board game. One word that sums up my impression would be "brutal". 10 Plays: I've only managed to win once. The taste of victory was sweet. I've been playing with random squad assignments, which I think may be adding to the difficulty. Still, I'm enjoying myself and would love to play this cooperatively a bit more.

RATING: 3
Random: The game

I see a lot of people comparing it to a puzzle, but what kind of puzzles relies so heavily on dice rolls? You also draw a card each turn to add more luck factor on that luck factor.

So the turn order is: 
1: Chose your action (you have two choice, no kidding...)
2: Execute your action. This often involves rolling a d6 (starting at 0, to 6) )with a 50% success rate
3: Monsters attack. Roll the die (maybe you'll be able to re-roll one or two times if you fail, depending on other players actions): 0-1 = fail... Higher might mean a fail too, depending on the enemies... Failing = you lose one of your two characters.
4: Draw a random event card that may ruin your game

Halfway through the game, one or two players probably got kicked out of the game because some die rolls killed them. They're now having fun playing on a videogame or something, you wish you were, too.

RATING: 7
I've played solo a few times.  It does a good job of having the cramped feeling of investigating a derelict space ship overrun by monsters.
The rules aren't too complex.  The action cards add a nice variety of actions.  The location and event cards keep the game feeling fresh with each play.  The fact that you can't perform the same action twice in a row keeps the game from being purely tactical.

I've done two coop games: 2 player and 3 player.  The 3 player was long and seemed 'easy'.  The 2 player was shorter (about 45 minutes) and semeed 'hard'.

The game is very luck driven.  And the '30 minutes' is a lie.  Its a 1 hour game.

I got a 5 player game in.  Still luck driven, but the 'shared experience' of playing the game makes it quite fun.  If you are looking for a game to win/lose then this won't cut it.  If you are looking for an enjoyable way to spend an hour with some friends then it may work for you.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
In this dice driven card game, you take control over 6 Space Marines from different orders with different specialties. You embark on a mission to fight your way through the narrow spaced corridors of a xeno-infested space hulk. 

The game is actually easy to learn, although I had some troubles getting into it. Once you are acclimatized to the artificial atmosphere, the game runs quite smoothly though. Your Marines can each take one action during your turn. This means you either shift your position in the formation (move), engage some of the xenos (attack) or support your allies. After that it’s the Xenos turn. That part is handled by the game itself.

In the end it is all about managing the phalanx of Astartes: Decimate the enemy, diminish risks and planning headings. One or two bad dice rolls however may lead to a gruesome dead of your squad all too early.

We all know that in the grim darkness of the far future there is only war... and despair. 
No seriously, I would not recommend this game to anyone who just wants to have a good time – you won’t find it. Unless you – like me – are looking for a brutal, ceramite hard challenge.
Because if you happen to beat the game, you are entitled to perform your best victory-dance.

RATING: 8.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I never played Warhammer 40.000’s tabletop wargame and neither did any of the Space Hulk boardgames: I’m a fan of the setting’s fluff though and I also GM a Dark Heresy RPG group. So when I finally had the chance to try out Death Angel didn’t let this opportunity slip: and I did well, for it’s a great strategy game, despite being just a card game with some die rolls.

What it really excels in though is atmosphere: Death Angel perfectly recreates the feeling of a boarding party entering an enemy-infested ship, facing constant dangers and struggling to succeed in their most holy task. Outnumbered but never outwitted let alone outgone, the characters (being the Emperor’s finest) have plenty of space for individual sacrifices, last stands and a wide array of «let’s push our way and go out of here quickly» situations, which make for a good narrative and an even deeper thematic immersion.

Playing Death Angel is such a rewarding experience that I’m confident my rating will raise even further soon.

RATING: 7
Likes:
   - Probably the most thematic card game available
   - Very cool artwork and graphic design on the cards
   - The engine that runs the game is very original and elegant

Dislikes:
   - Runs longer than it probably should
   - The decisions to be made are pretty obvious most of the time.
   - Since its not scenario driven, can feel a bit "Samey" after a few plays (expansions obviously help this a bit).

Notes:
   - The original box is a joke, and if you want to fit this game with any of the expansions + sleeve the cards, time to find a different box.
   - One thing i noticed is that the game play becomes much more interesting if you have previously played the Space Hulk miniatures game

RATING: N/A
Кооперативная карточная игра от Fantasy Flight Games и Кори Коничка.

События игры проходят во вселенной Warhammer 40k, на "корабле-призраке", вернувшемся в пространство из варпа.

Про Космодесант, зачищающий отсеки корабля от Генокрадов.

В основе заманчивая механика, подстёгивающая с одной стороны обсуждения планов и координацию действий, а с другой - самостоятельность решений. Реализовано тем, что все приказы раздаются картами, а те игроки держат втайне друг от друга. Даже те, что разыгрываются на текущий ход.

Выйдет этим летом.

RATING: 8
This is one my favorite solo games and hits the table more than any other of that category. I feel there are much better co-ops available, but really this shines best as a solo experience which is a rare thing. Ghost Stories might make for a good comparison. While gamers I respect love Ghost Stories, though, I do not; it seems like a puzzle which  presents situations which might be resolvable though it's not clear when they are or not. Death Angel is a difficult game to win and there are puzzle elements, but the theme coheres to the experience much more satisfyingly in my opinion. The puzzle elements in Death Angel really do smack of tactical decisions. The strategic decisions really do present you with choices to attempt risky gambits or try to open a couple more doors, hoping there aren't swarms waiting for you on the other side. It's no small thing to have pulled this off in a solo game that is so simple and brief.

Don't let the warnings of the bad rulebook scare you off. It isn't great, but it, combined with perhaps checking a couple of rules on BGG, is manageable. Once you have your first game completed, you'll never end up having to look at it again anyway as the game really is so easy to play. Death Angel is a real gem for solo play.

Update: It's down to an eight for two reasons. The evil of the game I find is better done with Ghost Stories and the quick solo play is better done with Friday. Still, it's definitely a keeper an one I look forward to playing when I want a little more theme and a short solo game.

RATING: 7
Otro juego descubierto gracias a Marc.
Se trata de un juego de cartas ambientado en el mundo de Warhammer 40.000. Es puramente colaborativo. Cada jugador controla uno o varios equipos de marines espaciales, que deben recorrer pasillos de una nave hasta llegar al destino final. Durante su trayecto, deben hacer frente a los alienígenas que salen por todas partes. En su turno, cada jugador debe escoger una acción para cada equipo. Hay tres acciones disponibles: mover y activar, apoyar, o atacar. 
Es un juego de cartas completamente diferente a lo uno puede estar acostumbrado. LAs cartas actúan como si fueran figurillas. El juego te mantiene en tensión, porque los Genestealers no dejan de aparecer. Además, es bastante rápido.

RATING: 7.5
Very fun, challenging co-op. The theme does nothing for me, but the game play is stressful and exciting. I like how the game changes as you begin to lose marines: on one hand, the game becomes much harder because you have more aliens per character to deal with, but the smaller number of marines means that they're easier to maneuver and control. It's awesome when you're able to pull off a narrow victory after losing an entire team earlier in the game. 

Despite the BGG stats, I'm not as crazy about the solo game, just because I find three teams to be too much to manage by myself. The two-player game is great, because you have just enough control over your own men for it to not be overwhelming/confusing, but coordinating the timing and actions with the other player is a real challenge. I don't think I'd like this with more than three people, however, especially with the elimination aspect.

RATING: 7
Good co-op game.  The rules are simple and the action is quick.  The first few plays are enjoyable but after a while it gets somewhat boring seeing the same cards come up.  It is a small card game, so I guess that is to be expected.  Obviously expansion decks would help with this.  

Another criticism I have is that it often feels like the game is "on rails".  The best decision for the group is usually somewhat easy to figure out, so it feels like you are just going through the motions of playing the game.  I suppose that applies to all co-op games to some extent, but it feels more pronounced to me in Death Angel - possibly because it is such a small, compact game with simple rules...there aren't that many decisions to make or unique tactical situations that arise.

RATING: 5
Space Hulk: Death Angel is a cooperative card-based game set in the heavily themed Warhamer universe. As someone who doesn’t play a lot of co-ops, who doesn’t enjoy many card games, and who generally despises science fiction themes, this was certainly not a well-made match. Despite my initial skepticism, I was pleasantly surprised by the game itself. 

One of the primary problems of co-operative games is that they tend to result in obvious decisions. Players approach those games as a bugger-like hive mind and view individual turns as interchangeable tools to advance the common good. Well-known complaints, such as that of the overbearing leader, are really just manifestations of this problem. Death Angel manages to do away with much of that difficulty by introducing both player elimination and simultaneous, secret action selection. Of course, those mechanics introduce their own problems. But giving players incentives to act in divergent self-interests and asking restoring the significance of the individual turn through simultaneous individual decisions is a neat innovation. 

The actual gameplay is procedural, fiddly, and about as far from thematic as games get. Still, it packs a decent number of semi-tough decisions into a short, panic-filled game. The game seemed perfectly designed to allow us to just scrape by until the final moments, when it overwhelmed us with swarms of some sort of death-eating science monsters. Or something. It was all black and purple splotches to me. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I love and hate this game, an oxymorn.  The game is a fusion of modern elegance and dated mechanics.  

The game has no difficulty setting like other Pandemic or Lord of the Rings.  There a steep strategy learning curve, more like a wall where most people will win out sheer luck.  However once you read the great strategy guide, Death Angel Complete Guide by Nano (Friman), the game is too easy.  The guide in bgg files section.

The AI, the script that controls the environment and the Genestealers are modern and so clever, yet there is player elimination like an Ameritrash from the 80's, is baffling.      

How bitter sweet...

RATING: 7.5
This is a fast, brutal, and very tense card game for 1-6 players. Very thematic, and the artwork on the cards is great. 

My only major gripe is that the rulebook is very poorly laid out considering how easy it is to play the game.

A smaller issue is the replayability factor. Yes, there are POD expansions available through Fantasy Flight's website, but unless you're really into the core mechanic of the game (aliens spawn around/beside you, you shoot them, rinse, repeat) they're not likely to add much replay value.

RATING: 7
I bought it because I wanted something to remind me of the old DOOM computer game.  I'm not disappointed.

This will have the same problems that plague a lot of co-op games - they can be very easy or very hard, though very easy is a relative term.  The rules are rather lengthy, but intuitive once you get in the flow of the game.  There is some risk management in which action you are leaving for subsequent turns, and which marines you put in the most perilous positions.  The decision space could be larger (since there are only two actions available after the first turn for each team), but the game accomplished what it sets out to do.  I will eschew larger dungeon crawls in favor of this little gem for the small footprint of the box alone.

As such, an early roll of bad luck can kill a game in a hurry. Also, the marine combos have widely varying degrees of value. Some marine pairs are close to worthless (at least in solo games), while others are "must haves" - that is, if you choose your marines rather than drawing the marine pairs randomly as per the rulebook.

Overall, a good game if you can set your expectations (regarding a win percentage) very very low.

RATING: 6
I am not a big fan of Warhammer 40K universe but the theme suits the game well. (rating +1) The 4 player game (8 marines) feels right: a squad of space marines rushing through a space hulk exterminating hordes of aliens, which threaten to overrun the squad. In solo games (6 marines) the pace is slower (and somewhat less thematic, IMHO): it takes noticeably longer to clear a location. However, slower pace allows more maneuvering. You have to accept, though, that regardless of the number of players, there is much randomness in the game: the best tactical plans can be ruined by a few bad rolls or unlucky draw of an event card. There isn't much that you can do to mitigate the risks. That said, I do not find the game too difficult: so far, marines have won more often than lost. Also, randomness should ensure that the game remains  fast and chaotic instead of being paralyzed by deep analysis. (I am thinking of introducing a sand timer to further reinforce the effect. :devil:) The game has nice components. The only complaint I have is that the art on genestealer cards is a bit too dark. (This does not affect gameplay, though.) I wish there was more more variety to the game, for instance, genestealers are bit too generic. Like all true co-ops the game is prone to be dominated by the most experienced player. The game plays very well in solo mode (I would rate the game 8 as a solo game).

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Components: There are way too many similar-looking components on the table for what the game delivers. This is a prime example of a game that obfuscated itself by trying to make all the components a deck of cards. The marines in the middle (who are all basically indistinguishable from each other) should be miniatures, as should the genestealers. The location cards should just be square tiles. There needs to be better color coding between the marines and their action cards; I could not tell yellow from orange to save my life (oh, wait, they all died).

Also, there is too much information spread out over the board in the form of text, between my own action cards, those of my teammates, that of the location cards, and the room card. At any given time I had no idea what the capabilities of my fellow teammates were.

Experience: There are some very clever mechanisms at play here. Thematically, I enjoy how we're all just marching through the room in a single column. The 'facing' aspect is interesting, as is the alternating choices to support, move, or attack. The location cards are cool.

But the game is very mechanical. Every round contains basically two decisions (in a three player game): which action cards to play. The rest of the activity is laborious to perform, but without being fun or tense to watch unfold.

Last Played: 2012-03-13
Eagerness to Play Again: Eventually

Plays (1):
3 players: 1

RATING: N/A
2014/10/09
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.8
[2011-03-07 Rating: n.a. -> 8.8]

Space Hulk: Death Angel (SHDA) caught me by surprise. I never played Space Hulk before and so the announcement of SHDA left me somewhat cold. This was until I saw it for a few bucks online and read a review of it to see if it is worth the money. Boy, was I lucky that I did so that day. Otherwise I would have missed a novel and clever game which, and this is it's biggest bonus, is a great solo experience.

Within SHDA you and your friends control teams of Space Marines that try to survive in a Space Hulk fighting of hordes of Genestealers. To win the game, you have to traverse a set number of rooms and fulfill a winning condition in the last room. This sounds easier than it is in reality. But it is even fun to lose in this game, as each round is really tense.

The great thing about this game is the clever approach that designer Corey Konieczka took. While I find that some of his game contain too many mechanics that detract from the main game, this one feels perfect mechanicswise: Each turn, you play one action for each team from a fixed set of three available actions. The action you played in one round can't be played again in the next round. While this doesn't sound like there is a lot to decide on a given turn, each of the actions comes with a special ability that breaks the rules in some way or another. And these special abilities are what makes the game so great. Each round you have to think of a clever way to combine them so that you won't get slaughtered.

Another great decision of Mr. Konieczka was the abandonment of a map. By the use of the formation, he got rid of all the complex stuff like Line of Sight. Instead, each Genestealer can only be in front or behind any given Space Marine. With a quick glance at the formation, you know everything you need to know to make an informed decision about which action to play. There aren't any unnecessary mechanics that detract you from the main course of the game.

Then there is also some luck in form of a die. Sometimes your best laid plans will get screwed by a bad die roll. But the more I played this game, the more ways to prevent these situations revealed themself to me. It's the clever use of your support tokens and the special abilities of your Space Marines that will save your day.

To sum it up, this is really a clever, novel and great coop-game. Even better, it is a great solo experience and this is the way, I play it most of the time. And the best thing about SHDA is it's low prize.

RATING: 4
A solo/cooperative card game based on the classic Space Hulk boardgame.  Players represent squads of Space Marines, creeping through a hulk trying to accomplish a scenario objective.  Quite straightforward game - players play a card to issue an order to their pair of marines - support, move, attack.  Orders are resolved in order, game controlled genestealers attack, then more come out to play.  Clever game - certainly tried hard to recreate the "feel" of Space Hulk in a card game format - ultimately however it's quite dull and repetitive, while the parent game is a white knuckled, teeth gnashing, anguish fest.  This game is also let down by a truly awful rulebook - such a simple game explained in a totally convoluted manner.  Still, if you can't get Space Hulk, this is worth a look.

RATING: 8
Fun, cooperative and thematic. You lead a squad of space marines through sections of a space hulk, fighting off waves of baddies as you go. There's a fair bit of luck involved with dice rolling and card randomisation, however strategy comes from deciding which squad will perform which action per turn (move, attack or support), using special abilities and planning ahead. 

People have complained about the poor manual, however I had no issues learning how to play the game.

One thing I love in games is theme, and this game has a lot of it. Plays well solo. Highly recommended!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This does an okay job of capturing some of the flavor of the Space Hulk board game, but is by no means a substitute (nor does it claim to be).   The presentation is a bit more colorful and cartoony than the dark gothic setting should be, but that's a general problem with FFG's presentation of all the GW properties.   The game play is very simple - each player has a pair of marines who can select one of three actions each turn:  Move/Activate, Attack, or Support.   Actually, you cannot choose the same action on two consecutive turns, so you really only have 2 choices each turn.   The rest of the game plays itself, and that's the main problem.    I'm generally not a fan of co-op games (and the auto-play is one of the main reasons), so your mileage may vary.   The price point is about right.

RATING: 6
A fun coop card game that delivers on the Space Hulk theme. Each player plays a pair of marines all lined up in order (this is Space Hulk after all) in order to travel through several locations and make their way out. The Genestealers appear in random order and position relative to your line so you all need to coordinate how to use your combination of abilities to combat the threats against you. Sometimes the only way is to sacrifice somebody (which is why you get two dudes, I guess!). The way you can use orders and play cards requires smart play and coordination among the team.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I really enjoy this co-operative card game where you are imperial space marines pitted against the hoards of genestealers.

I like that each different marine squad has different abilities (mostly based upon the weapon they carry) but it is a little disappointing that each squad has an affectionately named brother wound. i.e a generic spod. It might have been nice if each marine did something a little special rather than just one of the pair.

I like the facing mechanic and the re-roll ability which applies only if you are facing the gene-stealer attacking you, thus there are a lot of tactics to ensure your marines are positioned in the most effective formation and this doesn't necessarily just mean at the head of the column.

The terrain cards and varying objectives give a lot of replayability and the event card drawn by the player with the lowest initiative each turn is nice, I especially like the events where you must decide what is going to happen before you show everyone else the card .i.e you have to pick the squad the card will effect without discussing it with the group.

With a group that can work together well you can mitigate the luck of the die roll and maybe your marine will even survive!

RATING: 4
I've tried to like this game but it's just not for me.

I'm not a big dice roller but don't mind a bit of it in games as long as I have methods to mitigate the rolls. Limited re-rolls don't count for this in my book. This game does nearly, maybe, just enough to make me think that I am in control - decisions about which orders to give each turn, special card abilities, gaining additional re-rolls etc. And it's short enough that a few bum rolls don't spoil hours of careful tactics.

I don't mind the difficulty either.I enjoy the theme and the stories that can develop within the game. I had started to think of some of my marines as individuals, not just another card. For example, Sergeant Lorenzo is a f**king beast after the stand he made in one particular game.

What I'm not comfortable with is the event cards. The genestealer spawns are fine - the colour coding shows how likely they are to spawn at a location so you can priortise - but the actual events themselves feel a bit "Community Chest". I've spent two turns positioning my marines to cover every slot on each side...pull event....awwwww, every genestealer has now just flanked! Absolutely nothing I could do about that. I can't even be reasonably expected to guard against the chance that this 'may' happen in any one particular game.

And the rulebook sucks. You're constantly jumping around to try and work out what a turn involves. Classic FFG :) The game is quite straight forward but the rulebook makes it seem so complicated.

RATING: 8
As I hoped, this is a tight cooperative game which pits your characters against evil monsters of a kind. The setting is a huge space ship in the Far Future. Could as well be a medieval battlefield or ships on the Spanish Main - personally, I would have preferred such settings. 

Death Angel also is an elegant design, and I didn't really expect that. A single die is used quite ingeniously for two types of combat (attack and defense work differently) including all special abilities. It is abstract and feels thematic a the same time. The monsters are just stacks of cards, they don't even have stats - but are terrifying nevertheless. Locations differ only in limited features, some have a corridor and some a dark corner, most have a door and some a computer panel ... and still they feel more different than the rooms in many dungeon crawlers.

This game is an excellent design.

RATING: 7
I'm rating this primarily as a solitaire game.  I wouldn't enjoy this co-op, and seriously doubt my game group would either.  Even with the rule of not showing your hand, this is a game that is too prone to Alpha Player syndrome, or else everyone is just going to die horribly.  Also, with player elimination, whoever is first to lose their squad is going to sit out the rest of the game.  Games are fairly quick, though, but that's still an issue for a co-op game (Co-ops that have EVERYONE lose or win together, are what my family and group tend to prefer).  However, it's been quite enjoyable as a quick solitaire experience.  It will grow old fast, though.  In fact, after 2 weeks straight of solid play, it's already beginning to wear a bit thin.  Definitely going to have to pick up the Mission Pack.

The rulebook is the worst excuse for a "Choose your own adventure" novel that I have ever come across.  Page 7 tells you turn to page 25, page 8 might tell you to turn to page 16, so on and so forth.  I almost trashed this game because of the rulebook.  I stuck with it though, and found that the game mechanics were EXTREMELY simple.  It's a shame the rulebook is the worst I have ever seen.  I can't even being to imagine how many people it's turned off to the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I prefer this game as a solo game. It brings on the tension of an Aliens-type horde attacking a small group of marines from multiple sides. It is horribly difficult. I believe I've only ever won scenarios in which you have to push the button! Once one or two of your marines die...it's only a matter of time before the horde builds and they drop like flies.

Thematically great (like Space Hulk)...mechanically though, there aren't a whole lot of options. 3 per squad. And since you can't use the same squad action twice in a row...it's more like 2.

Multiplayer, this suffers from the alpha player syndrome. You're not supposed to tell others your actions. You're supposed to develop a sense of coordination through practice I suppose...but still...it's aggravating letting somebody do something that is not complimentary to what you are going to do.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.7
I own the game and the first two expansions, and I've put a serious amount of play time into this. It's simple enough that new players can understand the rules after 2 rounds or so, it doesn't take up too much space, and it's all played in a manageable time. On top of this, there's a lot going on in every play through, and it works surprisingly well as a solitaire game.

The mechanics match the theme well: every round, an overwhelming number of genestealers spawn in, and you must choose your actions carefully in order to survive. Do you want to attack and try to diminish their numbers, therefore making the defensive dice rolling easier? Or do you want to support a squad mate, which basically is like giving him an extra life for when the genestealers attack? Or do you want to interact with your current room's unique environment, which generally has some fairly interesting effects? To make your decision even more interesting, each of these basic actions comes with a special ability unique to the squad you're playing. Each decision drastically changes the game - there's no 'fluff' here, which is why I gave this game such a high rating. The amount of strategy and substance packed into such a short gameplay time is impressive. There's a LOT of strategy in hand management and card selection here - partly due to the fact that you have a very limited hand of cards to choose from, and once you use an ability, you have to wait a turn to use it again.

Genestealers pile up very quickly. They follow you between rooms, meaning that every time you fail to kill some by the end of the round they spawn in, you have that many more to worry about at the end of the next round - and the more genestealers that are left, the less likely you are to survive. It's when you're outnumbered by genestealers ten to one that the game really shines; you'll risk your best squad member by blowing up a promethium tank, taking out all genestealers he's engaged with, but risking his life in the process. You'll sacrifice squad mates left and right in mad attempts to achieve the game's unique win condition (which is different every game).

If your squad survives, they will generally do so by the skin of their teeth, with just one or two of your original team left. Obviously, because the game relies heavily on dice rolling, there will be some games where you steamroll the genestealers and there will be some games when you're wiped out a quarter of the way through the facility. But these games are still entertaining (the losing ones more so than the winning ones) and when you have a really close game it's like striking gold.

The game does a good job at making you feel overwhelmed, so that when you finally pull through, you feel like a god. Or, at least, a space marine - and that's a great accomplishment for a game of this size, length, and price.

RATING: 10
Lots of luck is needed to win the game but also a lot of skills. The game can drag for a long time when players do not know the team abilities, but turns into a fast game when everybody knows all the teams.

A lot of synergy is needed to maximize card effects, and there is always more things to do that can actually be done, resulting in tough choices each turn. Hope for the best, plan for the worst, seems to be the key strategy.

The teams are not balanced, so with 1, 2, and 4 players, the game difficulty can be nigh impossible or a walk in the park, depending on which teams are in play.

RATING: 6
Packs all the of the theme of Space Hulk into a card game excluding (critically and unfortunately) the shoot-from-the-hip pace of that classic title. I expect it will play well with adult gamers but who knows when it will hit the table? A lot of page flipping during my first game of what is at heart a pretty simple (but clever) design, and several questions remained unanswered even after the first play. A near miss now that may grow into something more as my lad's gaming tastes mature.

RATING: 9
This was recommended to me over the holidays in a forum post in which I asked for dungeon crawl recommendations that I didn't have on my wishlist (I know, I know). It's also a game I would have never even looked at twice had it not been mentioned, and my game life would have never known the fun it was missing.

This game is simple to learn, deceptively so, and do not let the simplicity in execution fool you. It will kill you dead. In fact, my last game ended with a single soldier left alive, five baddies ready to eat his face, three tokens on the final location card, and an activate card played in order to roll. I had been rolling zeroes for what seemed like the last half of the game so we were feeling good about our last chance when...

I rolled a five. A five. A DAMN FIVE. I WOULD HAVE KILLED ALL OF THE BAD GUYS WITH THAT ROLL. 

*head thump* *much laughter* *goes to bed and dreams of rolling like crap*

I managed to snag the last copy of this game at my local shop and the expansions had sold only the week before. I will keep my eyes peeled because this game is just fantastic. Lots of tension, lots of nail biting choices, all wrapped up in a little box and a deceptively simple mechanic. 

Love this game, will be ever grateful for the suggestion to try it.

RATING: 2
I got this by accident in a recent math trade. I was flagging anything that looked remotely interesting, and I forgot to remove it when submitting my final want list. When I saw that this was what I got I was a little disappointed, but I had read that it's a decent game, so I wasn't crestfallen or anything. When I received it in the mail I was even a little excited, since the prospect of playing a new game always gets me pumped. Of course that was before I knew just how bad SHDA is. At least I only traded Citadels for it.

First off, I can't get past the ridiculous theme. I mean, the Warhammer 40,000 universe is just stupid. It's all skulls and frowns and aliens with long tongues -- like the cover of a fucking Megadeth album. The play is tedious and fiddly. You move these space marines around in a line. For some reason the marines are all named Brother Leon or Brother Spanky or something, so you get a big dose of I-love-you-bro-go-army aesthetic along with the tongue-alien (and did I mention skulls?) artwork. Purple-skinned aliens called "Genestealers" (which sounds scary I guess, but what does that mean? Do they just want a blood sample?) spawn along different parts of the marine line and you fight them by choosing cards that let you do stuff and rolling a die. Then they attack you. Then something happens. They they move. They you draw a card, maybe? Who cares? Don't play Space Hulk! More important: don't fucking recommend Space Hulk! Just a giant turd of a game.

RATING: 8
This really is a solo game to me. I've played it cooperatively once, and it was fun, but it was not that much different from solo play, so I'd rather play something else that I can't play solo when I have other players available. But that solo play is rather awesome indeed. And the whole package (including all those POD expansions) is still very portable.

While there is quite some randomness, mostly due to the die rolls, but also because all the carefully laid out plans can get stomped by some unlucky event card draws, there's many things that can influence the randomness:

* The support tokens you get, and where you place them
* How you position the marines
* The special abilities of the combat teams

Particularly those special abilities are neat. While some are rather blunt (flamers and assault cannons do a lot of damage, that's about it), others (like the psyker, or also the power claws and generally the melee teams) are a lot more strategic in nature and really allow for finesse during play.

RATING: 8
This is a quite simple and fun game with a very present theme.  This is not the deepest game of strategy available, but it gets extra points for being portable and versatile (1 to 6 players!!!!).
Some of the essence of Spacehulk is captured quite well (swarming aliens, doors, formation...) and it's just a deck of card, but nice to look, inspiring cards.

My rating may decrease after the initial enthusiasm but anyway, this game is an excellent fun per dollar (or euro) ratio.

RATING: 3
Looks cool, cool thematics, lets' go kill some genestealers.

But the whole experience is really bogged by the fact that you only have TWO actions to perform each turn. And then the CPU kicks in and moves everyone around. The CPU can take awhile to perform too, which bogs the game down further.

My friend tried to defend it by saying that the choice between the two actions is very important... As for my rebuttal, you are choosing one of the two actions from two different factors.

1) How good is this action for me, and what can I be assured that it will guarantee to benefit me?
2) How luck based is this action? How SCREWED OVER can I get from playing this?

When my main action relies on me to NOT roll a 1 on a d6 or DIE, I get frustrated with this game and its amount of luck. You cannot account for this BS in this game, and it will have its way with you or you will have your way with it. I really don't care for this game.

What does this game aim to be? An abstract shortned version of the Space Hulk? Thematically it achieves this, and that's why I'm giving it a three. It fails on every other level.

RATING: 4
I listed Game Weight as Medium since I had difficulty teasing out what the rules meant. FAQs available online help, but the game is unnecessarily procedural.

In a word: fussy.

Game play does [u]not[/u] feel like a desperate struggle against hordes of genestealers, but seems rather like a series of procedural optimizations. The genestealer cards look great, but differently colored cubes drawn from a bag could just as easily have used to represent them.

I'm not calling this [i]JASE[/i][b]*[/b] or anything like that, but it does seem rather Euro-y with a die thrown in to add raw chaos and make it appear AmeriTrash-y.

Before you laugh at my opinion, consider this: [thing=6249][/thing], [thing=16496][/thing], [thing=30869][/thing], and [thing=3307][/thing] all have greater levels of chaos than this game. In other words, all those Euros contain greater randomness than SHDA-TCG!

To be fair, I did enjoy my second game more than the first, but it still seems like a cube-pusher using cards.

And it's not truly multi-player co-op, but rather a solitaire game that others can play with you. I'd call this a solo game and ditch the semantics.

Plus it drags on so long...

RATING: 8
An absolutely terrific distillation of the [i]Space Hulk[/i] experience as a card game.  A real nail-biter, tense and filled with hard choices and awful [i]almost[/i] moments.  (As any good co-op should be.)

There is a real sense of increasing claustrophobia as Space Marines are slain and the formation collapses in on itself; the way swarms of Genestealers shift and wheel to flank the cumbersome Terminators induces a delicious sense of being overwhelmed.

It is a game of grand cinematic moments—[i]after luring a great mass of the swarm into the proximity of an aeons-corroded Promethium tankage, Brother Noctis sacrificed himself to obliterate the foul xenos in a cleansing firestorm[/i]—as well as careful strategizing with teammates to interleave actions into a tightly choreographed dance of death.  When you pull it off, it's exhilarating.  (Most of the time you won't.)

[i]Love it.[/i]

RATING: 10
One of my favorite games of all time.

Portable, easy to set up, and very fun and challenging.  Some of the language in the rulebook can be difficult to understand at first, but is well worth grasping.

Great adaptation of the classic "Space Hulk" board game mechanics into card-only format.

EXTREMELY DIFFICULT TO WIN.  The words "Space Hulk" have become synonymous in my board game group with near-suicidal chances of victory.  But once you know how hard it is, it can be just as fun to see how long you survive.  Sometimes we all get a good laugh out of being massacred in the very first location of a game.

We do have one house rule that I highly recommend.  Theoretically, any stack of 5 or more Genestealers is an instant kill against any Marine on the Genestealer attack phase (because you have to roll HIGHER than the number of Genestealers in order to survive, and the highest number on the custom dice is a 5).  To even the playing field a little bit, my group rules that a defending roll of 5 is a "Critical Save."  In other words, a roll of 5 allows the Marine to survive anything.  It's not enough to save your butt all the time, but it increases the knuckle-biting and cheering when you have SOME chance of survival against overwhelming odds.

Just as fun solo as with 6 players.

RATING: 8
I used to be a huge Warhammer 40,000 fan, especially with the Blood Angels - those were my babies.  So when I saw this little card game for a measly $20, I had to give it a try.

My expectations were very low coming into the game, I must admit.  I was also very confused by the rule book (very poorly written).  So after watching some YouTube videos on how to play, I gave it a shot.  On a side note, this is how I discovered The Dice Tower and Mr. Vasel.

Man, was I surprised!  This game is tough, full of challenge and overwhelming odds, but it is simple, fun, and a great game for 1-6 players.  What I mean by that is it plays equally well with any number of those players, which is something I have yet to see in a game.  Tough challenge, very portable, quick, fun, you can't go wrong.

The only thing I seem to have issue with is that my friends after moving from California do not want to play it because of the theme.  Gamer snobs.

The art is great!

2017-01-31

I finally played the game again and it wasn’t a good experience.

The game is obvious but it is hard due to luck of the draw and luck of the dice. The idea seems great but the execution is very boring and repetitive. 

The rulebook could be a lot clearer. Art is good.

Bottom line, I have no desire to play Space Hulk: Death Angel – The Card Game again, luck decides everything. I will sell it. One of the worst cooperative games I have played.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Space Hulk: Death Angel was one of the games that got me back into board gaming.

Being a fan of Warhammer 40K I was reading about Space Hulk (3rd Edition) which was out of print and had gotten pretty expensive. Death Angel was easily available, had the same theme, could be played solo and was pretty cheap.

CSS!!!

This game is awesome.  I have played LotR:LCG a few times and like it a lot because it is a challenge to try to overcome what the game is throwing at you, and I like that universe.  S.H: Death Angel is very similar in principle, but is more streamlined.

This game is very thematic and grossly under-rated on the 'Geek, imho.
The rules are a bit of a chore for the first couple of games, as with tons of very rewarding games out there, but if you stick with it, its worth it.

RATING: 6

RATING: 7
This is a cooperative game that is very challenging without being impossible. The game requires that all players fully devote themselves to helping the team uncover its best course of action each and every round lest the genestealers spawn out of control.  My overall experience with cooperatives has been that usually one or two people do most of the strategizing for the group.  My first game session with Space Hulk was no different.  Consequently I am looking forward to soloing the next play of the game.

I've since soloed the game a few times and prefer solo play to multi-player play.  The game is not very forgiving if a mistake is made because the genestealers spawn quickly.  In the multi-player version there are more opportunities for players to make poor decisions.  Most notably, event cards with the INSTINCT keyword require the active player to make a decision without consulting the group.  My experience is that I don't agree with the active player's decision 60% of the time because the right choice often requires advanced planning.  Advanced planning requires everyone's input and agreement, which the active player doesn't have at that moment.  Consequently, I feel that I have a MUCH higher win rate when I solo than when I play with others.  

EDIT: 2 player games work well too.  My husband doesn't like the Event cards with the INSTINCT keyword. He thinks a pure cooperative (you win together or lose together) should encourage team decision making.  Personally I don't mind the INSTINCT keyword in 2 player games (assuming the other person isn't a moron).  I simply don't like to play with more than 2.  Bad decisions become inevitable and the games take FOREVER.

RATING: 8.5
I'll admit being intimidated when I opened the box.  There are a lot of different types of cards and several tokens, as well as a lengthy rulebook.  Once I actually played through a solitaire game, though, I felt like I understood the game.

Still haven't managed to play it with anyone else--my wife is uninterested, and we haven't had a game night with friends since before Christmas.  I'm hoping to introduce a couple of my college buddies to it next week, though, which may or may not change my rating.

Thematically, the game is fabulous.  I don't even like Space Marines, and I enjoy this game.  There are many fun cinematic moments.  Mechanically, it's a little clunky and takes some time to learn, so it gets knocked for that.  Still, I appreciate cooperative games--as much as I enjoy playing games, I am not hyper-competitive, and I like the idea of being able to work WITH my fellow players, rather than against them.

I wish they had thrown in a couple more Support tokens.  I feel like I run out of them way too often.  Then again, that's just at single-player difficulty.  I'm guessing that the game is significantly more difficult with more people involved.  Boy, I really just need to get my friends over here so we can try it out.

RATING: 6
[i]Note: My rating is based on the game's official solitaire rules.

The rating for 2+ players is[/i] [BGCOLOR=#FF33FF][COLOR=#FF33FF]_[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR][BGCOLOR=#FF33FF][b]4[/b][/BGCOLOR][BGCOLOR=#FF33FF][COLOR=#FF33FF]_[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR].

[hr]
[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Good component quality

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Small box

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Small price

[BGCOLOR=#339900][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▲[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] Extra amount of cards to ensure a better game balance

[BGCOLOR=#FF0000][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▼[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] The rulebook makes the game sound way more complicated than it actually is

[BGCOLOR=#FF0000][COLOR=#FFFFFF]▼[/COLOR][/BGCOLOR] A bit wonky as a multiplayer game (including player elemination)

[hr]
[b]Space Hulk: Death Angel[/b] is a really tough cooperative game which makes the players take tough tactical decisions on every turn. The game has unforgiving random elements (card draws + die rolls) and it's the job of the players to tactically minimise the risk the best they can.

The replay value is good, as the game comes with many different groups of Space Marines with unique abilities and a good amount of event cards (although most events are repeated in the deck). Most location cards exist specifically for being used with a specific amount of players to ensure a more balanced game - which means most of the location cards are indeed not used in a single game.

The game works great as a solitaire game, but its game design gets a bit wonky when played with more players. The rules state that players are not allowed to directly communicate which of their 3 available action cards they will play on a turn (which is thematically really strange) and that the actions are then resolved in order by printed-on numbers on the cards.

This is strange, as it makes the game even harder than it already is and players with a good memory will eventually crack this artificial obstacle, as the numbers can theoratically easily be memorised, especially because an action card which has been played on the current turn cannot be played on the next turn (so the choice boils down to 2 cards per player).

Another problem when playing this game with others is player elemination. As mentioned before, this game is really hard, so it is indeed possible that a player gets eleminated early on. There is nothing that the eleminated player can contribute to the game from here on, which is a problem. The game's length is indeed usually rather short (depending on the number of players), but it's still a problem and which can be frustrating.

I won't recommend this game to most people, but people who are looking for a challenging tactical solitaire game should definitely take a closer look -- especially if they are fans of the [b]Space Hulk[/b] board game, on which this card game is based on.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
It's an interesting small game that has some potential, but I consider that there is still space for improvement.

I really like how they attempted to convert a Dungeon Crawl into a card game. Thinking that the same process could be applied to other dungeon crawls like "Hero Quest".

I do not really like how the marines are placed. I would prefer having location cards where you could decide where you want to move your marine. It would have increased the feeling of moving in a ship.

The other things I did not like is the fact that you control a team of character. In our game, we controlled 2 team (3 players). This has the effect of not having the feeling of being in the feet of your character. I would have prefer controlling only 1 character, with some HP and a hand of cards unique to that character.

Some cards action cards give special bonus to one of the character in your team. Since your team members cards almost look the same, you do not see at glance that they are different. You really have to search for the character's name. I would have preferred a large Icon on the character which has a special ability.

Finally, the cooperative part is a bit better than "Ghost Story" which could end up as a 1 player puzzle. Still, in our game, we decided to discussed openly, if you normally play with hidden action cards, it would reduce the effect of being a 1 player puzzle. But since every team only has 3 cards, where 2 can be played, they can generally know what you are going to do even if you do not talk to each other.

There are some situation where a character special ability allows him to take a decision. If the information to manage is hidden, then yes it reduce the 1 player puzzle syndrome. But if the information is open, players would get a tendency to talk and share comments.

So in conclusion, it's an OK game, where the dungeon crawl conversion is interesting and that has some potential, but there is still space for improvement.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Neat little co-op or solo game with a solid theme that brings out the feel of the game.  There are some clever pieces to the game such as initiative cards which the person must decide without consulting anyone else.  Facing of the soldier plays a huge role and each soldier is unique with one member of each team having a unique ability.  I worry about replayability as there are only a few scenarios, but this is a fun game and plays quickly.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The rules are quite well written and organized.  I had to go back and forth a bit, though: some sections give details and are referred to from some main section.

On my first game, I strongly felt the effect of luck (1/3 chance of having an unsupported Space Marine slain by a "swarm" of a single Genestealer).  However, a better strategy might work.

I did not feel the same intellectual challenge as when playing Magic against Magarena, though: there are fewer powers, and combats are much simpler.

Would I rather play Magic (Duel Decks) than this, though?  I'm not sure yet: both games are very different, and I don't yet know how the multi-player game feels.  Looking forward to playing to taste the game a bit more.  I'm sure that I can discover interesting strategies.  I'm not sure about the tactical richness, though, but we'll see.

However, I do appreciate the game as a kind of puzzle: how can the game be beaten?  It's nice to even be able to try this anytime, since the game can be played solo.

These remarks make me wonder whether I would not like Summoner Wars better than SHDA: more powers, more tactical situations, more "geographic" freedom, a fight…  SHDA can be played with 3 players, though, so that's a plus.

RATING: 10
I mainly bought this game because I travel a bit. I needed a portable solo game to play. This fit the bill quite well. Cheap, small and playable with 1 to 6 players.

I've always been a bit of a WH40k nut, so this game hit me hard. I love the theme and the desperate feel of fighting against overwhelming odds. The game isn't very meaty, but enough for me at least!

The game's lack of depth is something that's starting to irritate me a bit after 47 plays. I have to see if it lasts 100 plays after all...

Update 30.10.2016

Raised from 8 -> 9. It has stood the test of time really well :)

Update 14.1.2017

Raised from 9 -> 10. It is officially in the Pantheon of great games now. Never ever during playing I feel like it's boring, only the setup is a bit sleepy.

RATING: 7
I like this game, but it took me awhile to figure out how to play. I like how things change with the flips of the cards, but I would prefer damage tokens rather than the one hit one kill. This is less of a problem because of the hit system, but it makes the game impossible when the enemies start to add up. Also some missions are as easy as hit one dice once with five tries. Other missions are kill twelve enemies to advance. The enemies are bland, with three pictures to represent all of the enemies. The expansions fix some of that, making the enemies harder and the players weaker, but it's less fun. There is plenty to this game, and the random room factor is either nerve racking or fun. I have played a few games, and enjoy it, but unfortunately it's not going to win many awards.

RATING: 9
[microbadge=419][microbadge=5792][microbadge=5389]

Scenario: make a card game that can, in 30 minutes or less, largely replicate the experience of playing Space Hulk.  This sounds near impossible, but it's pulled off with serious style in Death Angel.  The game is very hard, but that only makes it more sweet when you win.  Very unexpectedly, it plays equally well with any combination of one to six players; that sort of range is virtually unheard of.  You're unlikely to come up with a better game for its price as well.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Solo:  
GS 12 : 7 SM

~~~late breaking news~~~
Just read Friman's Complete Guide(highly recommended), and WOW did he put some thought into the game, and offers some great insight into this game.  If you are feeling it is too hard as I did, then check out his guide.  Before reading the guide I was winning about 20% of the time, which just isn't fun, and so was trying out some variants (see below).  Now I'll give some of Friman's thoughts and advice a try and see what my win ratio and more importantly fun ratio is before throwing in too many of the variants.

~~~~Later thoughts~~~~~
Friman's guide is very good, but geared towards 5-6 teams of marines against normal genestealers where he said he was winning 90% of the time.  In solo with 3 teams of marines against Tyranids, I think recently I am at best winning about 20-30% of the time.....which can sometimes be epic storytelling, but gets old after a while.  I think I need a break from it for a while....when I come back, I may try adding 2 support tokens for each support action.  Sorry, Friman, but the game (with Tyranids) is just too stacked against the marines.
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

Previous thoughts: 
Man, do I suck at this(without some below variants, I was only winning less than 20%).....had demoted the Green team to guard duty back on some backwater planet, until I started to use the variants below.  Will see how balanced it is.

Playing solo I was taking 4 teams and play with the 2p scenarios, but now trying the normal solo-play of 3 teams.  I like having more command with 4 teams, but like the shorter playing time with 3 teams.  I'm going to play some more with 3 teams to see which I like the best.

Solo variants that I am trying out from various forums: 

-Grenade(1 time use) for non-hero marine (can use once instead of normal attack(range 1): kills number on die(rolls can't be rerolled), swarm is then stunned and does not attack that turn.  If the marine is killed before using the grenade attack, the grenade is lost(may try adding a Terminis variant).

-Thunder Hammer/Shield heroes: when facing an attacking swarm, has a roll before swarm attacks that kills one GS on skull roll(may not be re-rolled)or blocks that one GS(if not killed)...then the swarm attacks(with one less strength...one GS was killed or blocked). Trying to make the Green team viable, and model hammer/shield from Space Hulk.
-Lightning Claw heroes:  when facing an attacking swarm, gets one attack when defending before swarm attacks (no re-roll)....as above, but does not get the block on one GB (no Shield).

-GS rolling 5 on an attack always misses....just to allow that rare event

-Last Stand: when a swarm rolls equal to it's size when attacking, the marine gets one last attack(no re-rolls).  If they miss then they die, but if they hit, the swarm attacks again with its reduced numbers.

-Terminis: in conjunction with the grenade variant above (or potentially even without it).  If the non-hero marine has not used his grenade yet and is killed he will drop his primed grenade and kill a die roll of 'stealers (first from the attacking swarm, and then from the other engaged swarm if there are two).  Of course, no re-rolls.

RATING: 9
I don't like most card games, but this one is decent.  I like both the theme and the game play.  Presentation and the quality of the materials is good.  If you are a fan of the James Cameron ALIENS movie you'll enjoy this game.

My only negative is the manual.  It's a flimsy booklet of just 32 very small pages.  While reading through and walking through a first game (or second or third...) you'll be flipping madly back and forth through the pages to figure out what step to take next.  I think that FFG could have written a much better manual.  I had to watch a couple of Youtube videos to clarify a few things.

RATING: 8
If there is one game in my collection that I love and hate in equal measures it would be this. The game design is fabulous. So thematic. You really do feel like a team of space marines fighting for every inch of your lives against ever decreasing odds, thanks in large part to that one red dice. But oh my, you really do need to be in the right mood to be slapped about by that dice! Don't pick this one off the shelf if you are wanting a nice laid back solo moment. If you die (and you will) then suck it up and either pack it away for another day, or shuffle that deck one more time brother!

Addendum: I own all the expansions, and honestly haven't begun to delve into them. The base game has been enough to satiate the Space Hulk in me...for now.

RATING: 8

The more I play, the more I like this game, so much fun, you will learn to know your guys by their names !

Still, there is a veat : it could be less fiddly. It's not that the rules are heavy, but with the special powers, the travelling phases, the event phase steps, i still make little mistakes in the flow of the game here and there. it's just that it's easy to miss a step at one point or another, especially if you're a bit tired.

Plus the setup is a bit long for the length of the game...

RATING: 9
Solitaire: I didn't really grok this game after a read-through of the rules, but within a couple turns on my first play, it clicked. I lost, of course, so maybe it didn't click all the way! But I like losing solo games; it motivates me to keep playing.

This is a fun game. There are plenty of levers to pull, but not too many; just the right amount. There's a palpable sense of dread whenever genestealers attack, which seems about right, and the game does a good job of expressing its theme: genestealers scuttle about, flank, form larger swarms, and are hard to eliminate entirely.

It's mostly tactical, but satisfyingly so. The balance of luck and skill is good, and the mechanic whereby you can't re-use any single card from round to round is just dirty.

The components are great, of course, and I'm glad it uses no half-size cards. I can see lots of replay value, what with variable events, spawns, locations, and team composition.

And perhaps most importantly, playing it makes me want to play it again.

RATING: 8.5
SOLO (Rahdo #2)
CO-OP (Rahdo #4)
THEMATIC (Rahdo #1)
My personal #2 solo game

This is a very solid game, though the difficulty is harder than most other card games. One will often find their marines on the losing side of the battle, which makes winning even more satisfying.

The biggest drawback for this game is definitely the rules. You'll often be forced into situations where you'll ask yourself "ok, this situation isn't in the rule book, what do I do?" After navigating to the forums for this game, I understand certain scenarios much better and have a better grasp on how to properly interpret a few card's abilities.

This is a SOLID solo game and a lot of fun. The artwork is top notch and really pulls you into the bleak situation of these marines. It's very fun to have to make decisions about which marine to kill off or who to attack and defend. Strategy is very much important in this game. While the roll of the dice does offer something in which you cannot control, using strategic maneuvers to have the dice roll in your favor is key to a successful mission. 

I definitely recommend this game to anyone looking for a card game that packs a punch and also requires all your concentration.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Though it can be played with more, Space Hulk: Death Angel - The Card Game is, for all intents and purposes, a solitaire game.  In it you assemble a team of space marines, a la the movie Aliens, to board a spaceship and fight off hoards of, you guessed it, aliens.

Once you have the rules down the game is actually fairly simple to play.  In a solo game you get three teams of marines to work with.  Each team of two space marines has one of three actions they can perform on a turn.  They can either attack, support, or move and activate.  After they take their action, the aliens will attack them.  This goes back and forth until either all the marines are dead, or they've made it through to the final area of the ship, and completed their objective.

For a small card game Space Hulk: Death Angel - The Card Game offers an intense experience.  Death lurks around every corner.  That sounds fun, right?

RATING: 8.5
I had my reservations when I first saw the material and the rules - but, wow, this co-op game does really work and captures the essence of its bigger brother well! Having no human opponent but the game only needs some random elements (otherwise the game would be pointless after "solving" it once). The luck swings by these randomizers, cards and a die, are not as terrible as they seem over the course of the game. Seems to be easier with more Marines (= players). I witnessed lots of sessions as a game explainer and saw player elimininaton most of the time only in the final stages of the game, as long as the group acted wisely. 
As the game mechanisms are very interlocked, it is not easy to explain and grasp at first, though basically everything is quite easy to play, after ALL rules have been explained.
Try to roll the die on a soft surface - I have witnessed that the die I have notedly "prefers" several results when rolled on a hard surface. Repeatedly having 6 Zeroes in, like, twenty rolls is no fun.

RATING: 7.5
Card-driven tactical game based on the Games Workshop 40K/Space Hulk licence in which you play space marines clearing out aliens from a drifting spaceship. Though playable with a group it works just as well as a solitaire. Session times for solitaire about an hour. 

What is remarkable about this game is that it through very clever spatial layout of cards and draft mechanics excellenlty captures the theme, mood and setting of the original game. Cards are laid out in a single file and can face two ways, capturing the narrow confines. You can be beset from any position and direction, and every choise you make is a hard one with consequences. The rules are complicated for a card game, but actually, just as complicated as they need to be to capture the setting, and not more than that. The game is difficult--very difficult!--but this too contributes to the desperate atmosphere of the game. In all, the theme/mechanics intergration is quite outstanding.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Game in a Nutshell: Co-op card game of Space Marines trying to survive close quarter alien attacks via a small hand of action cards and die rolling combat.

Played as: Solo

Played with: Base game, no expansions

Pros: For a plain-old row of cards, the theme actually shines through. It really can feel like walking into the bowels of hell knowing full well, as your marines are getting devoured one by one, that it's not going to get any easier. Does an excellent job of putting players in some very tough situations with interesting decisions to make. Quite challenging. The artwork is good. 

Cons: There is nothing intuitive or easy mechanics wise when it comes to this game. Too many niggly rules, an unnatural game flow, unhelpful graphic design, and a landmark achievement in poor rulebook layout all detract from what should be a quick immersive experience. Forget a reference card (of which there is none included), this game needs a flow-chart; how's that for fun in a small box thematic game? The game can often boil down to how well you roll the die.

Other: It's interesting that a card game could be more complicated than its boardgame counterpart. I almost never played the game, as the initial read of the rules was really that hard to stomach. After four plays, I still haven't made it through a game without needing to check for the 'order of events' or something else. Despite that, I'm still interested in trying the game multiplayer. My only fear there is, the time to play is only going to increase exponentially and the game will basically require someone to 'be the boss' to have a chance at surviving.

Best Use: Great if you want a lot of theme in a small box and don't mind an un-necessarily steep learning curve.

RATING: 5
After a couple solo plays, I must say this does seem like a rather dry logistics exercise. I've seen enough to reasonably say that, as a solo experience, it's about a five. Perhaps it's better as a multiplayer game, and I should have a chance to try that in the next couple weeks.

It's got a bit of the artificial Euroness that typically detracts from the immersiveness. For example, you can't take the same action twice in a row. Why? Because the cosmos requires play balance, that's why! If Euros have taught me anything, it's that you can't build a ship, hire a specialist, make babies or sell a red whatchamadoodle at the same time someone else does.

It's not quite enough of a Euro that it extracts my soul and stomps gleefully on it. But it's not really AmeriTrashy enough, given the theme. And no, the saying "best of both worlds" does not apply. The "best of both worlds" would be all AT, no Euro. Obviously.

I think that with a game called Death Angel--admittedly they were up front about it and called a card game, it says so right on the box--there should be more, you know, of a sense that you are being snapped at by the pointy claws and teeth of nasty death.

The rule book is a strange beast: reasonably well-written with good explanations and relatively clear rules. Yet a few bits of information are clumsily placed so that you have to flip to the back to make sense of something you are being told in the front.

It has a hefty dose of luck that can hose you early. This is not a big issue for me--I loves me some dice!--but it will drive Anti-Dice EuroBob to fits of madness. Even with just the one die! Exciting, isn't it?

The game is quite likely to confound the first-time player, because it so stubbornly refuses to be anything like what you expect it to be. It's probably best if you wipe your mind, have someone teach you the rules and get really shouty while you play it. You may love it or hate it or just feel a little blah like I did, but I don't think that mere words can prepare you for what a weird little morsel this is.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
