RATING: 9
[microbadge=1714]

[u]08-Feb-2013[/u]: This is one of my favorite games.  You command a team of Space Marines going on a mission to take down the alien Genestealers that have taken over a Space Hulk.  I knew nothing of the Warhammer 40K universe prior to picking up this game, and I still don't know much about it.  But I do know it didn't stop me from loving this little game.  It's mostly cards with a few cardboard chits and an Evil Red Die.

You line up your marines in a straight line formation and the enemy spawns on either side.  You must use the basic and special actions of the marines in the right combination to slay the creatures and work your way through a number of "locations" within the ship.  Reach the end and meet the final condition of that location and your mission will be successful.

There is a lot of strategy and tactics in this game.  There is also a lot of randomness as both your attacks and your defense is based on a single die.  However, by using the special actions of the marines as well as support tokens, you can mitigate that randomness, and even turn it in your favor.

This game is easy on the wallet.  It comes in a small box.  The replayability is fantastic, especially if you add in any (or all!) of the four expansions currently available.  The random set up and gameplay adds to this, as well as to the challenge.  It can be daunting sometimes, especially early on in those first several plays.  Eventually, if you stick with it, and learn from your mistakes, your successes will be fantastic.

I like to say this is the boardgame version of Aliens (the movie), when the marines go into the spaceship and are attacked by the aliens.  I play those scenes out in my mind every time I play this game.  I love it.

[u]26-Jan-2014[/u]:  Yep, still love this game, so I had to add it to the top of the list with Carc and Friday.  How could I not.  I'm still working (slowly) on my 100 Play Challenge.  I'm almost halfway there and still haven't touched two of the expansions.

While it may be somewhat similar each game, I just really enjoy the Aliens-like narrative that plays out each time I play this game.  So cinematic.  And the game is still tough, no matter how much experience I have gained so far.  I'm still finding new ways to succeed (and fail!) even now.

Combine this with the small box and a reasonable price tag....winner!

RATING: 7.1
A fine Games Workshop card game that is relatively quick and easy to figure out how to play - but which remains quite difficult to easily win.  Operating as a line of hulking Space Marine Terminators, clearing out hallways in a floating abandoned starship (a "space hulk" in the Warhammer 40k parlance) of insectoid Genestealer monstrosities, the game is an emulation of cramped quarters fighting and struggling to avoid precious losses in the face of enemy hordes.

I haven't played this game in a rather long time, as I think I overplayed it with people in New Haven.  Everyone enjoyed it, but I just got sick of it. Even still, keeping it on the shelves as an easily-transported and fun challenge of a game suitable for many different numbers of players.

RATING: 6
I received this as a birthday present and was most grateful that my chums knew me well enough to think that this game would suit me down to the ground. The premise is the same as [thing=54625][/thing] in that you’re a member of a small squad of space marines in ‘terminator’ armour (extra-super-duper heavy armour) making your way through a derelict spaceship to find and clear the objective room. The catch is that the spaceship is infested with angry, angry aliens (Genesteelers in [company=26][/company] lexicon) who want to stop you. And there are a lot of them. They are pretty dangerous with claws that cut through terminator armour very easily, but at least they don’t have acid for blood, so there’s that.

The game proceeds as your team clears each area and then advances. It’s a co-op and you all play against the game with a choice of around five or six from the eight or so marines each with various abilities. Then into the hulk you go, the game will control your surroundings and move the genesteelers about the place. From what I have seen it there is a fair bit of randomness in the movement so things don’t get predictable. This also adds a bit of tension to the gameplay.

I played with Mrs Fish and we tried to learn the game as we went, alas, the rulebook is not as well organised as it could be and several times we found ourselves confused and made a couple of mistakes which turned out to be pretty serious in game terms.

At the end of our game, in which we were slaughtered, Mrs Fish indicated that one play was enough for her for now. I kind of like the idea and want to play a bit more to see how it goes with another try, but I can’t see this displacing our other two go-to options for co-ops so when I get the chance I’ll try it solo and decide about it from there. 

Overall, it is a good looking little game, the components are all of excellent quality and the artwork very much fits into the whole 40k dark future sort of universe, but I’m just not sure how engaging the actual gameplay is.  I’ll give hang on to it and try to play a bit more on my own to really get across the system before I see if I can tempt Mrs Fish into another foray into the grim dark future...

RATING: 7.2
主題:1
利用擲骰、卡牌能力以及合作機制，來模擬太空船艙中陸戰隊員對抗議性的故事，玩起來很有電影異形第二集的味道，主題與遊戲機制很符合!

美術:0.9
紅色與鐵色所形成的灰暗世界，各有特色的陸戰隊以及形形色色的異形，美術很棒，與主題搭配的很棒!

規則:0.8 
就擲骰遊戲而言，本遊戲規則簡單，遊戲流程動作合理，規則好上手，沒有太多爭議的地方。

設置:0.9
設置方便快速，選好隊伍，關卡、怪物、事件，很快就可以開打。

路線:0.5
遊戲重點在小隊能力的互相搭配，看你想要打那種隊形，買了擴充小隊後，可以有比較多的變化組合!

互動:0.2 
雖然號稱可以多人合作打怪遊戲!但遊戲的格局我覺得比較適合單人指揮，跟朋友玩過一局，大家都不愛，但單人遊戲卻是刺激到不行，真的很有指揮小隊打異形的感覺。

個人:0.9 
關卡少了點，劇情變化少了點，但還是不失為有趣的角色扮演遊戲!

朋友:0.1 
推坑對象有限，遊戲不適合多人遊玩(因為容易陷入單人指揮大家的遊戲)會讓同伴缺乏融入感。

想玩:0.9 
可以連開好幾場，每次挑戰打異形都充滿著真正的戰鬥感，讓人很容易融入劇情。

收藏:1 假如沒有戰鬥擲骰的遊戲，這款遊戲很適合當作擲戰鬥骰的入門款!

總分:7.2
講評:主題鮮明，戰鬥過程緊張刺激，充滿著戰場上的不確定因素，是款個人非常喜愛的擲骰遊戲，但遊戲機制的關係，不適合多人同樂，除非桌咖也非常喜歡相關主題。

RATING: 6
A friend of mine who is a big fan of the Warhammer universe purchased this game, the Space Marine Pack 1, and Mission Pack 1 expansions.  He sleeved all the cards, then read the manual, and promptly packed it away.  When he learned that I enjoyed board games he brought it out of storage and asked if I could learn how to play, then teach him.  I took it home for the weekend and spent a night reading the rules and playing a couple of solo sample games.  I then took it to my FLGS and played with a buddy there.  My thoughts: I could take it or leave it.  There are some good things going on here, but altogether I think it is a lot of motion for not much game.  The theme works really well here with the concept of terrain in the location where your formation of marines are fighting.  Enemies spawn and you do battle.  That thematic integration carries the game pretty well, but in the end you are really looking at limited play.  You can make a choice to select one task among two options to use for your marines.  You then may have some follow-up choices, but in the end it is quite literally a roll of the dice.  I think my friend who is a Warhammer fan is really going to like this, but for me it didn't entice me into desiring my own copy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

I don't find any real fun in this game. There is a reliance on luck and dice rolling that I am not a fan of, and not enough ways to manipulate/mitigate that luck other than rerolling. The theme is pretty great, but the game itself just doesn't do anything for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Owned and unplayed. I need to find someone to teach this to me. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
When a game uses dice, it by the nature of dice, introduces randomness.  It is not likely that you can roll 6 times with a 50% chance of hitting and miss every time.  But, dice do not care about what is likely.

This game, so far, from what I can see, hinges completely on die rolls.  Yes, you can mitigate the effects and probabilities.  And you must do so to have a chance.

The question about such a game, is not whether the die makes a difference.  Rather, does the way the game plays make it worth while in spite of the rolls?  Is it fun and interesting to attempt to mitigate the die rolls?  I'm not sure yet. - update: Now I am.

I do find the effort worth the risk.  After playing several games, I find the journey to be exhilarating.  I carefully craft (read AP) my tactics, trying to mitigate the risk of short term losses in order to plan for the victory.  Every time I have a string of bad rolls, I do not find myself discouraged.  It really feels more like a challenge rather than a setback.

It is amazing how much variation has been packed into just a few elements (i.e. you can do a LOT of different things with just 2 marines, 2 facings, and 3 cards with 4 actions).

I am fortunate to have found yet another solo system that does not feel like the game is playing me.  I would have to say that this system is really smooth.

Why this is not a 10:
-> I do not want to play this all of the time
-> The theme is not my favorite
-> While the variations are amazing, they are not as complex as the games I favor the most

RATING: 8
Brutally difficult co-op/solo card game. It is a touch more fiddly than I'd like--on a given turn (solo play) you might select 3 cards, shuffle some Marine cards around, fiddle with some tokens, discard some baddies, roll some dice, shuffle some baddies around, draw new baddies, flip a room card, refresh terrain cards and blip piles, and repeat.

That said, it's one of the better games I have for solo play. Getting to the final room as the lone surviving Marine barely hits the objective is exhilarating.

RATING: 7
Un bon petit jeu "portable" puisqu'il est dans une petite boîte stylée. Et pas n'importe quel petit jeu puisqu'il s'agit ici d'un jeu de coopération avec un thème WH40K Spaces Marines vs GeneStealers (genre de créatures moitié humaines moitié Alien®). Il va falloir survivre jusqu'au bout du vaisseau Space Hulk pour venir à bout de la mission.
Ce que j'ai beaucoup apprécié, en plus du fait que le jeu soit dur, mais pas trop, c'est la gestion de la coopération. Les joueurs jouent cartes non visibles et ne doivent pas révéler leurs cartes mais uniquement la stratégie globale qui sera mis en oeuvre avec l'escouade. Il y a égalment un système d'event qui ne doit pas être révélé par le joueur qui le lit jusqu'à ce que ce même joueur choisisse, seul, la ou les cibles de cet event. J'ai trouvé cet aspect vraiment original qui pallie grandement au problème de l'effet leader des jeux de coopération.
Il y a une grande rejouabilité puisque les lieux sont tirés au hasard bien qu'il n'y ait pas beaucoup de scénarios différents selon le nombre de joueurs.
Le facteur chance est aussi bien géré avec les différents pouvoirs de chaque binome de space marines.
Un bon jeu à tester au moins une fois si on aime les jeux coopératifs.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Very in-depth thought in German language: https://www.unknowns.de/wbb4/index.php/Thread/7914-Space-Hulk-Todesengel-Betrachtung-als-Solo-Spiel-und-vielleicht-ein-bisschen-meh/

10/2010
Overwhelmingly negative reactions from my friends after the first play (5 players): The game fell flat because of 
- "too much randomness" (game description suggests you can plan well, but it's actually rather limited), 
- quick player elimination ("What? Now I'll have to sit and wait for half an hour?!") 
- very few tactical options and boring combat system ("Rolling the dice is just like throwing a coin!"). 

I personally liked the game feeling, and I think it's really okay as a filler (although it might take too,long to play), but as long as I'll be playing with my current group, I am sure the game won't hit the table soon again.

UPDATE 08/2012
I still enjoy the game, though I doubt that it is suitable for 4 or more players. The marines get killed really quickly, resulting in early player elimination. Could factually become an unintended solo game.

Rule book is badly structured in the usual FFG manner. I think I'm going to rewrite it soon, strictly putting the rules under the respective step.

RATING: 5
Hard to grasp rules, as I find often the case with Fantasy Flight rulebooks, which tend to make the games harder to learn than they should be (kind of like letting the computer science guy write the how-to-use manual). Not a good sign when a rulebook lists two editors and both of them somehow missed the spelling of "seperate" under "Setup". More to the point, however, the explanation of rules, even the setup, are unclear (pages 21-22, the explanation of spawning Genestealers, is a perfect example, as, if I was deliberately trying to connfuse people about this rule, I couldn't have done a better job than what's printed--only when I found a setup video did I understand what was meant), so I would expect that many players should expect a longer-than-necessary learning curve for a game rated complexity 2.4 (as of July 15, 2014). I'm also not encouraged by comments of some Geeks that the quality of playing the game isn't worth the effort of learning it. Purchased, December 2012.

RATING: 7
規則:
*洗勻異形跟事件卡蓋著，選對應人數的起始設置卡，挑對應數字的地點卡隨機抽然後疊起，在腳色卡放完後，根據設置卡設置地形卡，然後根據地形卡下方數字放對應數目的異形卡蓋著形成blip牌庫放在左右兩側，抽一張事件卡，放對應的異形卡在對應地點(事件卡不結算)
*隨機起始輪流挑一個戰鬥隊伍標記，3人以下挑兩輪，然後拿對應的腳色牌跟所有行動卡，所有腳色卡洗勻後在起始地點下方擺成一列，上半部的面左，下半部面右
*遊戲進行數輪值到完成最後地點卡的對應條件，或是到達最後地點卡時消滅所有場上跟異形牌堆blip卡，全死就輸，每輪有四階段
1.每人一起選取要執行的行動卡蓋著，不能選上回合作的
2.照行動卡數字小到大執行
>支援 放置一個支援標記到任意腳色卡上，攻擊或防守如果有面對異形時支援標記棄掉可重骰一次
>移動 可移動該小隊的每個腳色卡跟相鄰腳色卡換位置一次，只有該小隊的可換方向，然後可啟動面對的地點卡能力，每張地點卡每輪只能使用一次
>攻擊 所有同小隊腳色可攻擊面前的異形卡，然後丟骰，骰到骷髏面成功選一張棄掉，攻擊距離代表可攻擊相鄰行，1可攻擊相鄰1的
*特殊能力行動卡除攻擊跟協助外，不管面向哪都能使用
3.異形攻擊階段 同疊的異形攻擊同行的腳色，從最上方開始結算，左到右，每次攻擊丟一次骰，數字比異形卡數多就沒事，小於等於則腳色卡移除
4.抽事件卡結算 最後行動的抽，有instict的事件該玩家要決定玩執行，不能討論，之後結算下方的效果
*起始設置卡下方標示主要(左)跟次要(右)翻異形卡的數量，事件卡最左事主要生異形的顏色地點，中間是次要，從對應的blip卡生，沒卡就不用生
*異形移動時根據事件卡旁的圖案，一疊內有一隻有對應圖案就移動，上下的方向根據腳色卡上的標示
*殺掉的異形卡形成棄牌堆，不夠抽在洗勻
*特殊異形卡，必須是該棄牌堆中最後被移除的，如果該疊攻擊時，骰值-1
*當左右blip牌堆有一疊空時，則進行團體移動，之前的異形卡保留原位置
>用目前最上方的新地點卡取代舊的(不要蓋掉生怪數目標示)
>棄掉之前的地形卡，放置新的地形卡，根據地點卡指示放置
>棄掉之前的blip卡根據新地點卡放置新的
>結算地點卡進入效果
*如果有腳色卡被移除，上下哪一區的行數較多，較少的往多的合併，如果有已經攻擊過的異形卡先放異一旁等其他攻擊過在合併，這也可能導致地點卡的合併
***3人以下規則***
*2~3人時每人選兩組，1人時選三組
*選卡階段，每組選一張

RATING: 5
One of the more boring co-ops I've played. You control two guys each, and they're mixed and spread along a long line. Baddies appear at various points along the line. Basically you've got to kill them, so each team plays a card to either move along the line into killing range, or try to kill (roll a die at 50%) or play a support function to get support tokens out which will help with defence or future kills. Then the baddies roll dice to try and kill any team member it's next to, then more baddies come out and/or move in a really fiddly gamery non-thematic way (you say the corridors move towards each other if he dies? huh?), rinse, lather, repeat. Because it's meant to be frenetic corridor killing action, it's thematically correct to limit the amount of communication teams can have, but you can do some clever things if you move / action in the right order. Sometimes. Usually it's obvious what to do with your powers so there's little sense of key decision making, ie that you're dramatically influencing the result with your decisions. The end-game condition belatedly appears and it can be easy or ridiculously hard depending on how things have gone to date, so there's another random blow on top of all the random die-rolling which characterises success or failure throughout. To finish off, the rules are a mess as well, and the game usually plays long, so this is for those that are thematically blinded.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Talk about your Kobayashi Maru of Warhammer 40K! This game kicks your butt! But I love the atmosphere of the game. The mechanics seem intuitive once you,ve really got the rules down. Winning, however, is a different story. You really have to think and cooperate your way through to survive as long as you can. Much replayability. This one is a keeper, for me.

Rules are confusing; need many readthroughs. This is a game better to learn directly from someone; thanks for the video tutorials people have made.

I love this game, but here is what may turn people off:
the puzzly strategies for survival, the violent atmosphere, the awesome gruesome artwork, the deadly results of dice rolls, and the confusing rules.

RATING: 6
What I like:
- Very Portable
- Clever mechanics, and good use of theme
- Difficult decisions and short/long-term tradeoffs

What I don't like:
- One roll of one die can kill half your forces
- Took WAY too long with 4p (95 minutes after rules/setup)
- Player elimination
- Theme of religious military warriors

My first solo game took 100 minutes (I made it to the last room, although possibly by accidentally cheating a bit). My next two solo games took 30 minutes each. Maybe I had a rule wrong in the first one.

I don't love it with 1 or 2 players, because I don't like to control just one pair of marines. But with 4 players it took 95 minutes, so that was no good either. Maybe 3p is the sweet spot?

I'll go along with the BGG-voted weight of 2.3 Once you know the game, it's pretty smooth.

RATING: 6
Have only played solo and the rules are pretty badly written in places - luckily the rule book isn't a magnum opus so after the first few games I'm pretty much sure of 95% of the rules.

Since I can only comment on solo play I'll simply say this...

The game is fast, nailbitingly tense and very thematic. I can imagine the uneasy terminators knee deep in xeno body parts and their bolter's barrel blackened and smoking in the dim, flickering light of the cold metallic hulk corridors.

At times it can be a really hard decision choosing which card to play and even though the game relies almost entirely on luck, if I lose the game I don't feel short changed, it just encourages me to ready another squad of terminators and embark for the hulk once more.

Recommended for those who want a space hulk fix without the months of effort of collecting, painting and finding an opponent. I was playing this within a few hours of it's arrival!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
It's great to see a version of this game packed into such a small box. While this is obviously a very different game to the original Space Hulk, it does capture some of the same feeling.

The biggest change is probably that it plays as a co-op game and supports a range of player numbers, so nobody needs to play the part of the Genestealers (for those gamers who would prefer things this way). Of course, that may be a negative for those who enjoy playing as the aliens.

The way the Action Cards provide each Combat Team with different abilities is quite clever and doesn't over-complicate the rules. There are also some nice ideas in the terrain cards. However, I would have liked to see a little more variety and quantity of both location & terrain cards for repeat plays. Maybe there are plans for future addons...?

For a card game, it can take up quite a lot of table space, though this reduces slightly throughout the game as marines enevitably fall along the way.

The rules are a bit jumbled with way too many references, but fairly clear after a bit of effort. There is a lot less setup involved than the board game version and the game is fairly streamlined, so it can move along quickly - as long as you don't tgake too long mulling over who will do what this turn! There are plenty of small decisions, so enough to keep your interest, but not too much to bog down.

Components are excellent, although I would have preferred the card art to be a little brighter and/or have more contrast. Depending on lighting conditions, it can be tough to tell some of the Combat Teams apart as their colours are dark & quite similar. Also, the only other important pieces of information on the Combat Team cards are the marines' names & their attack range, both of which could have used a slightly larger font.

The dark borders on the cards isn't an issue once they are sleeved.

SLEEVES...
http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/554389/card-quality
"FFG suggest 3 packs of their green colour-coded sleeves as can be verified on page 4 of the manual (available on their website), and each sleeve can fit a card of size 56 X 88 MM"

RATING: 5
Update, Feb 17, 2011

This is staying at a 5. Awful, awful rules. I first learned this game at a convention, with only ourselves to learn the rules. Because of the awful rules, the game left a very bad impression.

I then finally played this again with a big fan of the game who explained the rules properly and clearly. Big difference, since this is an simple game to play.

As a co-operative game, it does its job; most players are actively involved in deciding what to do. You usually don't have too much of the Scotland Yard syndrome in which one person directs all the action. I think this is the case because each player has three action cards with unique powers. I don't think anyone is patient enough to find out and remember the powers for every player. Hence, people have to talk ...

Even though the game presents a compelling puzzle to solve (and co-operative games are just that, puzzles to solve as a group), the luck factor is so huge. Perhaps that's the point of the game. I suppose there's some entertainment value of watching the game/system totally annihilate you.

To be fair, I'm not a fan of Fantasy Flight Ameritrash games. At least Death Angel is short and not that rule-bloated.

------------

2010-11-29: Very, very fiddly card game.

The core of the game is about managing a queue of cards representing all the players' space marines. All players are using their limited actions to manoeuvre this queue so that they can better attack monsters on both sides of this queue. This itself is an interesting challenge, but because almost everything in the game is represented by cards, it's quite cumbersome visually.

RATING: 8
Birthday present. Have played three times (solo) and have lost twice (close calls) and won once (only lost a single marine). Note sure yet if the game relies too much on luck, as my win seemed to be down to a fortuitous mix of good dice rolling and helpful events at just the right time. Had loads of fun, considering I was playing solo, so current rating is an 8, pending further plays.

UPDATE: Have now played some two-player games. Yes, there is loads of luck involved, and some games are a walk in the park because the dice is on your side. Game is still great fun, very tense, very thematic. Some people will hate the chaos but I really enjoy this game.

UPDATE UPDATE: Played some three-player games. I am not sure how much skill (if any) is involved. There are definitely choices. And you can play "well." But playing "well" doesn't mean you win. It means you lose less spectacularly.

RATING: 4
The most frustrating conga line you'll ever take part on.

Decision space is essentially limited to 2 options per squad per turn. Luckily, that doesn't matter, because it's all going to be decided on the roll of a die anyway! Why bother? The game is mostly tactical, since with few exception of support tokens and room features, you are essentially reacting. But (a) things can shift dramatically from a turn to the next and (b) several of your actions "lag" (need to be set-up turns in advance). You can probably see how this can lead to a lot of frustration...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Death Angle is franchised from the infinitely superior Space Hulk board game, a practice that annoys me a great deal as invariably the new game has nothing in common with the old one.
Rather than a tactical wargame for two players you will get a solo to six player co-operative, somewhat lacking elegance as it is a Fantasy Flight game. It is a reasonable co-operative, and has an interesting 'instinct' mechanic which forces players to make their own decisions (some co-ops often end up with the best player at the table just taking everyones turn for them). On the other hand it has a military theme, and a lot of the success of co-ops (think Pandemic) is they appeal to the sort of people who doin't like military themes.
I've played a few solo games through and established that it is a purely tactical turn by turn response game, in which the Marine player is trying to maximise his kills of genestealers. The game as balanced seems a little too easy, I suspect it needs to be adjusted by some sort of 'bravado' rule in which players bid for how many extra genestealers there are at the start.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
[b]Gifted away December 2014[/b]

I've only played solo.

[b]Good Things:[/b]
:d10-1: It's thematic. Even though you're Marines aren't physically moving across the table, it really feels like they're advancing and fighting through a large vessel. Genestealers come pouring out of the ducts at the most inopportune locations. The event deck helps a lot.
:d10-2: I like the tactical feel. Each combat team is different, and each marine within the team is different. Some have special abilities, some are regular line marines. These differences give the player many decisions to make when planning his turn. The decisions feel meaningful and tie in with the theme.
:d10-3: The game is challenging. There are no guarantees a player will be victorious. Death for the marines will often come abruptly and even when the odds are in your favor.
:d10-4: Playtime is fairly quick; just about right for what the game is. It does not drag on with routine and monotonous decisions. 
:d10-5: The game is fun. Blasting genestealers, pulling off big kills and surviving improbable odds while making the right tactical plays is exciting. By the same token, losing your marines to bad luck or when they miss easy shots adds to the tension and theme.
:d10-6: The game will occupy hardly any space on your shelf. Don't worry about needing to get rid of one to make space for this.

[b]What isn't entirely positive:[/b]
:d10-1: Some players may not enjoy that one bad die roll or a series of rolls can overwhelm your good tactical decisions. It may feel too luck based, or bad luck based.
:d10-2: Setup time takes longer than I would like. Even though the game comes in a tiny box, it seems to take longer than it should to separate the different decks and the few counters.
:d10-3: Learning the game rules, processes, and mechanics may be difficult due to the way the rulebook is written. While I don't find the rulebook to be bad, I also don't think it was written as effectively as possible. I have a lot of patience for rulebooks, though I know others don't have the patience for a rulebook that is not clear & concise. It will likely leave new players scratching their heads & constantly returning to the book to search out an answer to a question about game flow or mechanics for the first several games.

[b]Conclusion[/b]
I don't have any play time in with 2 or more players. My experience, and comments above, are based entirely on solitaire plays at this point. I do believe this is a great game at a great value for $20 or less. It should offer many players a good deal of replay value. I recognize the theme, luck based mechanics, and rules will not suit everyone. But I think thematic gamers, card gamers, and solitaire gamers will more often than not find something to enjoy & appreciate here.

RATING: N/A
[color=#CC0000]

Rule book is bad.  Rule book is bad to the point of being prohibitive to young, inexperienced, or impatient gamers.  I can't give a copy of this game to my nephew who would likely enjoy it very much because he'd never get through the first turn.

  I'd wager 50% of the copies sold are never played due to the entry-barrier presented by the initial exposition of the core concepts of the game.  I received a second-hand copy that came to me super-clean, apparently never played.  That's a lost sale.  I should own a copy that was purchased new, especially at this price point.  250 people should not be looking to trade this game.

FFG needs to reach the conclusion that [i]the rulebook [u]is[/u] the game.[/i]

The game itself appears to be solid, a multi-player true cooperative with a lot of thematic elements and plenty of options to choose from.  The artistic aspects of the package are unified and beautiful.  The rules were too small and too terse to make determining which cards were which easy and understandable.  First-time setup on this game took entirely too long.

The cards themselves would have benefited from labels indicating what they are.  Here's a tip -- if it's an "event deck" consider writing "event deck" on it.  Trust me -- no one will mind.  This is how you move a new player into a game.  This is how you establish a relationship with a new customer.  This is how you sell games.
[/color]

RATING: N/A
Very enjoyable and eventful both played alone and in a group. The setting is easy to imagine and the mechanics don't get in the way. I like the instinct cards, they're a good way to keep everyone involved. In part they prevent an alfa-player from taking over because everyone will likely get to make decision with those cards. You could even ensure that easily and houserule event cards to be drawn in turn by everyone instead of the 'active player' being responsible.

The only downside is the rather small number of different locations you'll see. There are lots of combinations, but few single locations are memorable.

In the end, it's a co-op, and those have been shown to have low mileage with me. It's one of the best, most enjoyable ones I've played, but it's still a co-op. And, fun as it may have been played alone, I don't want to play alone. I'd rather do something else then.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I love this game. It's actually really simple. There's a lot of strategy, although once you figure out the techniques, your choices each turn are fairly clear. The luck is very real, but you don't feel that you have no power. It's hard as balls, and rightly so. Sometimes you have a freak game in which your dudes walk over all opposition and you win with 0.00% casualties. And you're like "I'm disappointed in you, game." Then you go back and play again. And everyone is dead but for one guy by the second room, and he's covered in 20 tall stacks of aliens on both flanks and you're thinking "That's more like it." 

And, crikey, is this game epic when luck and skill come together. When it's down to the wire and your three traumatized, viscera splattered warriors are facing off with the mother alien and her minions, and your Swordly Sergeant single-handedly faces down the charging horde and swords them all to death in a stream of skulls, it's incredibly exhilarating. You're basically cheering him on. 

And it is skill. Placement. Full awareness of what each Space Marine is used for. Making sure the grunts get killed first. Some are your cleaners, who hose down the foe. Some are your armored tanks, who can stop towering masses of Genestealers on their own. 

I had one game in which we were down to our last legs, with two survivors in the toxin pumping station. My shield and hammer sergeant and my psychic force-barrier dude. And they were up against a 20+ tall stack of aliens. And had to kill them all to win. And we did. By bouncing the grotesque foe back and forth between energy wall and metal shield, and chipping away. 

The Blood Angels are all unique and useful in certain situations, and they all die like flies when things go south, which they do, and often. But you can still win, with enough guts and brutal efficiency. But you can always still lose. And with even a smidgen of imagination, inspired by the Alien series or 40k, it's ALWAYS one hell of a story.

Excellent solitaire play.

RATING: 6
Got this for Christmas (2010) and played it 4 times yesterday.  3 losses and 1 emphatic win.  It's an impressive design - so many ideas packed into a little box.  As others have mentioned, success is highly luck dependent (as it is in the boardgame as well), and it can be painful to lose a marine on the first roll of the game (vs. a single gene-stealer).  But there's also a significant dose of strategy involved, and the decisions you make absolutely affect the outcome of the game.  When to attack and when to save your attack for a subsequent round becomes a crucial issue.  At first I didn't understand the power of doors, but in my one win, they played a prominent role in my success. I can see myself pulling this out every couple weeks for a couple quick solitaire games.

Update:  I still like this game.  As predicted, I pull this off the shelf every now and then when my schedule permits and play a couple rounds solo.  Always tight and very satisfying to win.  Haven't bought the Print-on-Demand expansions from FF, but mostly because they're clearly overpriced.

Update (Dec, 2012):  I might be over this game.  The last couple times I've pulled it out, it's just felt a bit too fiddly for what it offers.  Some of that FFG over-design getting in the way.  Thematic, sure.  Tough, you bet.  But not getting as much solitaire play-time as I thought it would.

RATING: 8
2013: 8. Really impressed with this game's design, packing the feeling of fighting aliens in tight corridors into a card game. The "spine" of marines is really brilliant.

I think the game works best solitaire, I have more fun that way.  Adding more people is ok, but because the game is so "small" in scope and play area on the table, I think it's terribly easy for one player to completely take over the decision making.  No fault of the game, I just think it's better for one player.

2014: 8. Have been playing the game more often lately after a long time sitting on my shelf.  Picked up Tyranid pack and have been experimenting with other game variants/house rules: the "token flips dice up one or down" rule to help mitigate the brutal randomness of the die; tokens can be used regardless of facing, and the fire team "drafting" rules to balance weaker and stronger teams. (see forums)  Feels good with these modifications.  Still best as a solitaire game though.

RATING: 9.8
This is the game that shifted my acquisition priority from multiplayer games to single player games.
The game play was clever and used innovative mechanics (at the time) to saturate you with atmosphere.
You quickly grew to empathise with the marines you controlled, participating in their struggle against the horde and sharing their triumphs.

Although the luck of a single die roll is normally a bad thing, in this case it allowed you to feel the thrill of suspense, anticipation and release without breaking you out of the narrative.
You are still able to think about your decisions, weighing up the odds to choose the best path, but knowing a resolution is coming in a single blow.

This was the first game to demonstrate the fraudulent idea behind trying a game once to see if you like it or not.
I was honestly thinking this was a complete luck-fest for my first few games and that it would fill a gap now and then. 
However the theme appealed to me enough to keep me playing through the losses (and wins), which then enabled me to discover some luck mitigation strategies.
Hint: [i]You really need to be aware of all the information presented to you when playing, and think everything through.[/i]
When I started winning more than losing, it became my favorite solo game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
3 solo plays, with Red/Yellow/Blue teams

Kind of a cool design, but just not for me since:
- I don't like cooperative games
- I don't play solo
- I don't know anything about the game universe
- The randomness of the d6 rolls can be somewhat annoying!
However, I may play a few more times, just to test out the other teams.

Each player plays a team of 2 marines; if playing 1-3, play with multiple teams/player. Every team is a unique pair of marines, with each one having its own special ability. The game requires you to travel through several locations (random subset of cards) and accomplish whatever the final location requires. Along the way, you'll face swarms of Genestealers who appear in random order and position. The trick is to figure out how best to use your particular combination of marines to survive (or sacrifice the less useful ones as needed!). And, you need to manage your hand(s) so that the formation (all the players) is able to maneuver and attack as needed every turn (each team has 3 orders, but may not use the same one in successive turns). Surprisingly, you do get a bit of the feel of a tactical game as you play out the turns!

The rules are fairly clear, but jumbled in a way that makes it a bit difficult to get through those initial plays correctly. A better player aid would have been great!

RATING: 4.7
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sEwuYoyHXaw

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a completely card-driven cooperative game set in the Space Hulk universe.  In it each player plays a set of space marines that are lined up in the center of the table.  Each round the players will play one of 3 cards from their hand to move, support, or attack aliens.  Then the aliens attack back and an event happens before repeating this process in the following round.  The goal is to kill enough aliens to progress through 4 different locations.

I've heard it said by many people in the industry that we are in the midst of the boardgaming Renaissance.  I tend to agree with that statement.  The industry is big and growing each year.  There are tons of outlets to use to produce and discover great games and even more outlets to get any and all information you could want on any game.  Why am I bringing this up?  Because this is a fine game.  And with so much available to us in this day and age, "fine" is a failing grade.

There are just too many good games out there for this to be anything more than an "also ran".  Granted, this game was produced 4 years ago but that simply means that while it might have been a good game once upon a time it just didn't remain competitive in today's boardgaming environment.  There's just not enough here to hold my interest past more than one play.  Each round is so formulaic and sleepy.  You just play one of only 3 cards and roll a die a couple times, rinse, repeat.  The cards are varied among players and do some interesting things...the first couple times you play them.  But you play them over and over and over again, they lose their flair really fast.

All of the combat is decided with the roll of a six-sided die.  No modifiers, the only thing you can do is spend a support token to re-roll.  If you hit an alien it dies, if the alien hits you, you die.  This isn't exciting or tense.

Speaking of not tense.  I think the worst problem is that this game commits the cardinal sin of cooperative games.  It's too easy!  I never felt in danger of losing and we went through the first half of the game 100% clearing the locations between rounds and not losing a single marine.  Out of 8 marines, we finished the game with 6.  Cooperative games need to beat you up a bit to be interesting, in my opinion.  Otherwise my eyes wander and I start looking at the clock for when it's over.

Like I said, there's nothing really BAD about it, it's just not something worth playing next to the hundreds of other coops out there, dozens of which are much, much better.  Once you know what you're doing this game does go quickly and it is all just a deck of cards so it has a small footprint and is portable.  But other, better games also fit these criteria.  I don't see any point to it unless you are a huge Space Hulk fan.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I'm not gobsmacked by Death Angel, but I like it. You could even say I find it addicting: I played 14 times in the space of 5 days. With a collection as large as mine, that's saying a lot.

If I were trying to find fault, I'd say that the basic tactical situation doesn't vary as much as I'd like, and that there isn't much actual movement. Theoretically your marines are moving, but the successive levels come to them rather than you physically moving them towards the new levels.

There are other small points I could quibble about, but they are all from a simulation perspective, and this isn't a sim. What it is is a small footprint, quick playing tactical game that captures the Space Hulk flavor well and provides an excellent challenge. It more than carries its weight given the small price tag.

My rating and comments are based entirely on solo play, but the game does support up to 6 players. Even if I never play it with others, Death Angel is sufficiently worthwhile solo to have earned a permanent spot in my collection. Recommended.

RATING: 6.6
6.60 from 34 buddies

Wishlist level 2

"Chris Brua(cbrua)
7

Another criticism I have is that it often feels like the game is "on rails". The best decision for the group is usually somewhat easy to figure out, so it feels like you are just going through the motions of playing the game. I suppose that applies to all co-op games to some extent, but it feels more pronounced to me in Death Angel - possibly because it is such a small, compact game with simple rules...there aren't that many decisions to make or unique tactical situations that arise."

"Ben(chally)
5
One of the primary problems of co-operative games is that they tend to result in obvious decisions. Players approach those games as a bugger-like hive mind and view individual turns as interchangeable tools to advance the common good. Well-known complaints, such as that of the overbearing leader, are really just manifestations of this problem. Death Angel manages to do away with much of that difficulty by introducing both player elimination and simultaneous, secret action selection. Of course, those mechanics introduce their own problems. But giving players incentives to act in divergent self-interests and asking restoring the significance of the individual turn through simultaneous individual decisions is a neat innovation. "

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
If you'll pardon the pun, there's good bang for the buck here. Space Hulk: Death Angel is a cooperative, card-driven, kill-the-nasties dice fest similar in feel to Ghost Stories. In many ways, its a puzzle game, with players trying to figure out how best to stay alive and eliminat the baddies with the options and abilities available. But where I don't like pure puzzle games, discussing options and tactics in Death Angel is a blast, and a large part of the attraction here. Given that each team has only three actions from which to choose each round, there is a surprisingly wide range of tactics the space marine teams can employ ... almost to the point of analyis paralysis on occasion. But generally things move along at a good clip, and players feel thoroughly engaged. The theme is strong and works well with the mechanics. In fact, this little card game captures much of the feel - and tension - of its older board game brother, Space Hulk. My only real quibbles are that the rulebook is just awful, making a fairly simple and straightforward game far more difficult than it should be, and that the genestealer artwork isn't all that dramatic or threatening. Other than that, Space Hulk: Death Angel is a winner on a number of fronts, including box size, price, ease of play, tension, player interaction and plain old fun. I'm starting this with a conservative 7 rating, but I look forward to playing more and expect that mark could go up a notch or two.

RATING: 8
Initial thoughts following first solo play:  wow.  If this game would've come out before the blazingly chromed reprint, I might have saved a hundred bucks.  It really is a very good representation of the board game, complete with agonizing tension and all.  But it's all represented in cards and a few chits, so it costs a pile less.  

Getting through the first play was harrowing for me, maybe because it has been so long since I ran through a new rule book.  But after it got off the ground, and in spite of a few hiccups, it is almost dynamite.  I'd love to get more plays in, both solo and with a few pals.

UPDATE:  4 plays, 4 losses.  This game is absolutely fantastic at both crushing your spirits and giving you small doses of thrilling triumph.  I'm about ready to proclaim it one of the top 5 games I've played in the last year.

2011-11-06 -- I actually re-bought this game! After seeing much conversation about it, I realized I didn't give it a fair chance. The rulebook is WIDELY criticized; rightly so. It's horrible. If you don't want to have a long, slow session with difficult referencing to the rulebook, then either avoid this or make sure someone else teaches it to you.

I will say, though, once you've got it down, it does make for a decent solo experience--this coming from someone who thrives on good PvP interaction in a game.

I've upped my rating from a 5 to a 6.5.

1/8/12 -- Alas, I think I'll be trading/selling this game off once again. It just doesn't call my name. I think it may be too long for what it is. I can set up Gears of War: The Board Game and play it in nearly the same amount of time. GoW is a superior experience for its components and streamlined play--not to mention my GoW minis are beautifully painted thanks to my Secret Santa (Christmas 2011).

RATING: 8
Another solid game by Corey Konieczka. Set in the Warhammer 40,000 universe, the players work as a team of Space Marines against the Genestealers aliens. A a tough battle it is!

The ratio of Win x Loss is low, but I don't mind this at all: I enjoy the challenge. And the game is fast enough so that the losses don't hurt that much.

The mechanics can get a somewhat fiddle for a card game, but I think that this happens because we tend to expect little work when playing a card game. It is easy, once everyone understands their options, to get the game going.

So, to summarize: a good game indeed!

RATING: 4
03/2012:4
I admit I am not much of a solo gamer. But this game intrigued me since I am a closet Warhammer fan.

There is one word to describe this game: tough. It is not easy to slog through a game without heavy casualties. While the mechanics are interesting and rather complicated for a card game, I can't help but feel that getting a space marine killed with one lousy hit kinda takes away something from the game. However, 

I really enjoy how the location, event and terrain decks interact to add flavor to the game. Being able to activate panels on terrains and how they interact with overall goals is neat.

Have to play with several more people, but I bet you the game will be even more random and chaotic with guys moving and switching around the formation.

RATING: 9
This is the only game I've given a full 10-point rating on Board Game Geek so far.

I never thought I'd like to play a card game or a board game solo. I tried this one solitaire to learn the rules so it would be easy to teach to my friends and became addicted. 

Death Angel is complex without being complicated, but the rulebook is poor/unclear due to poor organization. You can learn the game from it, but I recommend using Universal Head's printable rewrite at Board Game Geek. This makes the game easy to learn quickly. ( 

Death Angel is very difficult to win. That's part of why it's fun. It's a challenge. Luck is involved, but making good tactical choices is much more important than luck. Luck is mostly your enemy, something to plan against rather than something you're hoping will help you. This creates an awesome sense of dread that feels somewhat like playing a survival horror version of X-COM. 

The cards are very high-quality and harder to damage than the cards in most games. They feel nice.

There are expansions but I find them totally unnecessary. The game will keep me entertained for a very long time without them. I don't think I'll stop playing this for years, though I won't play it every week, or maybe even every month. If someone asked me to play it every week though, I don't see myself turning it down. It's highly replayable and great fun.

However, if you want to expand it, there are a few expansions available (get the Tyranid one if you only get one.) Also, there are fan-made expansions here at the Geek.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
As a solitaire game, this isn't too bad.  It takes a game to really get a sense of how the turns flow, but by the second game, you shouldn't have to refer to the rules too often.  It has a touch of Dungeon Lords, what with the "select a card this round that you can't use next round" rule, and a heaping helping of Arkham Horror/Battlestar Galactica with the event cards.  It's relatively thematic, for a card game, though it really can't compare with its pappy, since it had the miniatures and all.

As for the cooperative game, I'll have to hold off on rating that for now.  For one, I haven't played the game other than solitaire; for another, I'm not sure if I still like cooperative games as much as I used to.  Either way, I'll pull it out to play with the other FFG fanboys and see what they think about it.

RATING: N/A
Players choose from six different combat teams, each consisting of two Space Marines with different abilities. Each player receives three Action cards for each of his combat teams. After all of the Space Marines have fallen into formation, prepare for the first wave of Genestealers!
\13\\13\
Game play is quick and easy-to-learn. Each game is played over a series of rounds, broken up into phases. During the Choose Actions Phase, each player must secretly determine which of the following Action cards they wish to play on their Space Marines: Support, Attack, or Move + Activate. You can't pick the same Action card next round, so choose wisely!
\13\\13\
Action resolution keeps all players involved while the overwhelming odds inspire them to work together to survive. The Action Resolution Phase consists of each player revealing and carrying out their chosen Action. The lowest number card goes first, which means Attacks are resolved after Supports. Support tokens enable Space Marines to re-roll, so make sure to cover your fellow Blood Angels!
\13\\13\
The Genestealer Attack Phase happens after all the Actions have been resolved, so hopefully you thinned out the swarms since you have to roll higher than the number of Genestealers in the swarm to successfully defend. Finally, an Event card is drawn to spawn more alien adversaries. Once all the Genestealers have emerged from the darkness, its time to move forward, drawing a new location card. And then it's back into the fight!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Won: 1
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I have been thoroughly impressed by this unassuming little card game from Fantasy Flight. I'm not sure how Corey Konieczka managed to distill the mighty Space Hulk down into a deck of cards, but this fairly simple 30-minute card game feels every bit as epic as a three-hour run through a Descent dungeon. From the scenario cards to the combat team formation, there are just so many clever design decisions found in this game. I'm also completely astounded by the game's consistency. Every game seems to play out a little differently, yet it always manages to come down to an exciting and climatic ending. It really is a work of art.

If the game has any weakness, it is the multi-player rules. I don't think two or three player Death Angel is nearly as much fun as the solitaire version. This is very much a puzzle game and an unforgiving one at that, so having half of the Space Marines out of your control can be very frustrating. Also, you are only playing one action a turn for each squad. If you aren't controlling all of them, the game can drag a bit with some turns leaving you to feel like there aren't any real decisions to make. Player elimination is also a threat when playing with more than one, so again, I think this all adds up to Death Angel being far more effective as a single player experience.

RATING: 7
Surprisingly fun cooperative game in a tiny box. I love tiny boxes.

When you read the rules to this one, it sounds too simple--each round, each of the six squads can choose one of three actions and that's basically it. Ho hum, right? What makes it work is that each squad has wildly different and powerful special abilities to go with each of those actions. These abilities are often tied to a particular marine, making some more valuable than others--this is great since it makes positioning very important. Also, the way the single combat die is arranged to complement these abilities is very clever.

Fun to play solo, but definitely shines with buddies. It's a lot easier to sacrifice marines if you're controlling them all, for one thing, and it's just more fun to puzzle out the best actions cooperatively, when everybody's got their own abilities at the front of their mind.

Space Hulk: Death Angel captures the sci-fi theme and tension of its big brother, the mighty Space Hulk, in a compact card game.  And also resembling Space Hulk, this card game features very high quality components, with especially good artwork on the cards.  There's no board and the entire box can fit in your pocket (cargo pants pockets anyway), so this one travels nicely. RATING: 7.78
That game has the feel of the boxed miniature game: same squads, same atmosphere despite the loss of pseudo-3D. Game mechanisms are easy to learn and get used to, and each game is fast paced (solo game only for me). Each space marine team has its own special abilities making every one of them very useful and some combos can be exploited. It is in fact easier playing solo since the player can chose each action card knowing all other ones.
It seems that the game is hard to beat (have not managed it myself so far) and relies a lot on the randomness of the die. Needless to say, each space marine lost makes it even harder to go forward and the final stages of a typical game sum up to confronting one side's luck to the other's. The more space marine available, the more attacks possible and the lower chances of a hit from the genestealers. It requires however many support tokens in play at that time, and even then comes a time when a marine will be attacked while flanked.
The game material is great and helps a lot for the atmosphere, the size of the box makes it easy to travel with, and the duration of a game is such that games last for only a few dozen minutes. Replayability is high as long as one mixes the space marine squads before each new game.

RATING: 3
quality components, but a turd of a game

Rulebook is a total disaster. Theres thirty pages of rules questions here on bgg....

Its a good idea but the execution couldve been better.  Theres many confusing concepts with very few examples and some of the terms are inconsistent or placed in very odd places in the rulebook.

The game itself really boils down to a die roll to see if your guy survives, way too much luck involved, there are ways to re roll dice but there are times when you simply have no chance.

I enjoy a challenge but this is too much, maybe I'm doing something wrong, I just can't tell cause the rules are a mess.

Cool theme though, I want to like this cause I can solo play it but right now I don't like it at all.

RATING: 8.25
A cool 'puzzle' game that captures the spirit of the Space Hulk game. It's very good to play solo, since it's quick to set up a game. The game is hard to win but a good team composition should make you win most games. There can be annoying dice rolls especially at the beginning of the game were 1 genestealer kills a marine. But when you get going the luck gets more mitigated. 
With two players the game is also very nice. I wouldn't recommend to play with more if there are newbies in the group. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
An interesting co-operative game that delivers some neat, new ideas but doesn't quite have the impact or staying power of Pandemic or Ghost Stories. The system is extremely brutal, killing Space Marines left and right with wild abandon. I think part of the problem is just that: in Pandemic, the tension builds slowly to a crescendo. In Ghost Stories, you are slowly overwhelmed, gradually losing your life, feeling yourself fading away. In Death Angel, your guys just die. No growing weak, no feeling faint. Rolling a die = you're still alive OR you're dead. I'm not saying you roll a single die and the game is lost, but since you're losing the characters that represent you (or are supposed to represent you), it is somewhat detaching.

Own the first two expansions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
